<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-health">COMMUNITY HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Prepared by Samaki David Kithi</p>
<p>A student at Kenya Medical Training college- Mombasa campus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction-and-concepts-in-community-health">Introduction and concepts in community health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-and-concepts-in-community-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Goal: Give overview of community health</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Define the key concepts and terms used in community health</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain determinants of health</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe community entry process</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community - a group of people who share some important feature of their lives and use some common agencies and institutions. Community is a specific group of people, often living in a defined geographical area, who share a common culture, values and norms and are arranged in a social structure according to relationships that the community has developed over a period of time.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health - a balanced state of well-being resulting from harmonious interactions of body, mind, and spirit."</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community health - is defined by meeting the needs of a community by identifying problems and managing interactions within the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Population – a group of people living in a geographical setting in a period of time. Population can be described in terms of:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cohort – group of people born in same period. They grow together in same age group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk group - Some population groups are at considerably higher risk of contracting disease than others. These include infants, children under five years of age, pregnant women, patients with HIV/AIDS, as well as non-immune migrants, mobile populations and travellers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Density – is the number of people living in a square kilometer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Needs for health services – Health services such as immunization, examination, treatment etc. are basic needs of every individual, family, community or entire population.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Demand for health services - Every individual, family, community or entire population has a right to demand for essential and quality health services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Primary health care – e interventions that focus on the individual or family. Aare essential health services such as immunization, health education, nutrition and food supply, treatment and control of minor illnesses etc.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Risk of diseases – Exposure to a disease. Some risk exposures are drug and alcohol consumption, immune-suppression etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Aims - improving the health of a community range from improving access to medical care to public health communications campaigns. The aims of community health are:</p>
<ul>
<li>To bring essential health services closer to the community members</li>
<li>Empower community members to initiate, implement and own activities promoting their health</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="determinants-of-health">Determinants of health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#determinants-of-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Economic determinants including income, employment and working conditions;</li>
<li>Social determinants including social support, safety in the home and community, participation in civic activities and healthy child development; education and literacy</li>
<li>Physical environmental determinants including the state of the natural environment, the presence of environmental tobacco smoke, availability of transportation and affordable and adequate housing; and</li>
<li>Other determinants such as personal health practices, health services and biology and genetic endowment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="determinants-of-community-health">Determinants of community health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#determinants-of-community-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Community development - The community development process is based on the philosophical belief that people and communities are entitled to have control over factors that affect their lives</li>
<li>Group - People who interact and share a common purpose or purposes. There is no clear distinction between a group and a community except that groups tend to have fewer members than a community</li>
<li>Community health standards - Promoting health; Building individual and community capacity; Building relationships; Facilitating access and equity; Demonstrating professional responsibility and accountability</li>
<li>Community Engagement - is the process of working collaboratively with and through groups of people affiliated by geographic proximity, special interest, or similar situations to address issues affecting the well-being of those people. It is a powerful vehicle for bringing about environmental and behavioral changes that will improve the health of the community and its members. It often involves partnerships and coalitions that help mobilize resources and influence systems, change relationships among partners, and serve as catalysts for changing policies, programs, and practices</li>
<li>Cultural Influence - Health behaviors are influenced directly by elements of one's culture. As a result, social norms and other elements of community culture provide a potential tool for disease prevention and health promotion. Culture involves "the integrated pattern of human knowledge, belief, behavior, and material traits characteristic of a social group". An individual's culture influences his or her attitude toward various health issues, including perceptions of what is and is not a health problem, methods of disease prevention, treatments for illness, and use of health providers.</li>
<li>Community Participation - Concepts concerning community participation offer one set of explanations as to why the process of community engagement might be useful in addressing the physical, interpersonal, and cultural aspects of individuals' environments.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Community Empowerment - Mobilizing and organizing individuals, grass-roots and community-based organizations, and institutions, and enabling them to take action, influence, and make decisions on critical issues. It is important to note, however, that no external entity should assume that it can bestow on a community the power to act in its own self-interest. Empowerment takes place at three levels:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Individual,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organizational or group, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community levels.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Capacity Building - Another set of organizing concepts that can help guide approaches to effective engagement involves the process of capacity building. Individuals and organizations can gain control and influence and become players and partners in community health decision-making and action, they may need resources, knowledge, and skills above and beyond those they already bring to a particular problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community Organization - A "process by which community groups are helped to identify common problems or goals, mobilize resources, and in other ways develop and implement strategies for reaching goals they have set</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-health-services">Community health services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Community health elements are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Promotion of healthful living</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevention of health problems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treatment of disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rehabilitation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluation and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Research</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The services are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Child health services (Immunization and Growth monitoring)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maternal services (Family planning, Antenatal, Postnatal, Health education)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treatment of minor illnesses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health promotion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Referrals and follow up</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-health-standards">Community health standards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health-standards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Engagement</li>
<li>Participation</li>
<li>Ownership</li>
<li>Sustainability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-entry">Community entry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-entry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to the process of initiating, nurturing and sustaining a desirable relationship with the purpose of securing and sustaining the community's interest in all aspect of a programme.</li>
<li>The process, principles and techniques of community mobilisation and participation. This involves recognizing the community its leadership and people and adopting the most appropriate process in meeting, interacting and working with them.</li>
<li>Process involve:</li>
<li>Knock and enter upon response.</li>
<li>First greet chief and elders. Introduce yourself to the chief elders and other local leaders.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Inform them of your work with them.</p>
<ul>
<li>Ask for their permission and advice and state your mission e.g. getting information about the village or introduction of new health programme.</li>
<li>Thank them for their co-operation.</li>
<li>Identify contact persons</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="millennium-development-goals">Millennium Development Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#millennium-development-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Millennium Development Goals (MDGs) are eight international development goals that were established following the Millennium Summit of the United Nations in 2000, following the adoption of the United Nations Millennium Declaration. All 189 United Nations member states at the time (there are 193 currently) and at least 23 international organizations committed to help achieve the following Millennium Development Goals by 2015:</p>
<ol>
<li>To eradicate extreme poverty and hunger</li>
<li>To achieve universal primary education</li>
<li>To promote gender equality and empower women</li>
<li>To reduce child mortality</li>
<li>To improve maternal health</li>
<li>To combat HIV/AIDS, malaria, and other diseases</li>
<li>To ensure environmental sustainability</li>
<li>To develop a global partnership for development</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="problem-solving-in-community-medicine">Problem solving in community medicine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problem-solving-in-community-medicine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>What is a problem?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Problems are opportunities to make some good things happen. If it weren't for problems, what would be our motivation to create change?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Problems are also challenges. They call upon the best of our abilities, and ask us to go beyond what we thought we could do. They make life interesting, and, at least sometimes, fun. Without problems, life could be pretty boring.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Problem solving process:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="step-1-problem-definition">Step 1 - Problem Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-1-problem-definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Before you are ready to take any steps to solve the problem, you first have to be sure that you are clear about what the problem really is. It can be easy to get distracted by solving a different problem than what is actually causing distress if it is easier than dealing with the real problem. This step involves thinking about the following questions:</p>
<ul>
<li>How is the current situation different from what I actually want it to be?</li>
<li>What do I actually want, or how do I actually want things to be?</li>
<li>What is preventing me from achieving my goals, or from things being the way I want them to be?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="927fccdd">Step 2 – Problem Analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#927fccdd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Once you have defined the problem, you need to think about it from different perspectives to insure that you understand all the dimensions of the problem.</p>
<p>The following questions can be useful to help you analyze the problem.</p>
<ol>
<li>How is this problem affecting me?</li>
<li>How is this problem affecting other people?</li>
<li>Who else is experiencing this problem?</li>
<li>How do other people deal with this problem?</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5d3e568b">STEP 3 – Establish your goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5d3e568b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Once you have looked at the problem from different perspectives, you can decide what you want to achieve and establish your goals. You need to answer the very specific question – “What is my immediate goal?”</p>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improve my time management skills</li>
<li>Complete assignments on time</li>
<li>Improve my grades</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bb9ddb7">STEP 4 – Generate possible solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bb9ddb7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>During this stage the goal is to generate as many possible solutions as you can.</li>
<li>Do not worry about whether or not they are realistic, practical, or effective.</li>
<li>Be sure to write down all the possibilities you generate so that you can approach this task systematically.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f5b16126">STEP 5 – Analyze the solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f5b16126" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During this stage, you will examine each alternative and write down both the advantages and disadvantages to each. Some considerations to keep in mind include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Is it relevant to my situation?</li>
<li>Is it realistic?</li>
<li>Is it manageable?</li>
<li>What are the consequences – both good and bad?</li>
<li>What is the likelihood that it is going to help me reach my goal?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7f888343">STEP 6 – Implementation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7f888343" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The last step is to implement the solution you have chosen. This step involves identification of all the steps necessary to implement it, and also on-going monitoring of the effectiveness of the solution to make sure that it actually solved the problem. During this stage of the process, ask yourself the following questions:</p>
<ol>
<li>How effective is the solution?</li>
<li>Did it achieve what I wanted?</li>
<li>What consequences (good and bad) did it have in my situation?</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-contributing-to-the-success-of-community-engagement-efforts">Factors Contributing to the Success of Community Engagement Efforts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-contributing-to-the-success-of-community-engagement-efforts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Environmental</li>
<li>History of collaboration or cooperation in the community</li>
<li>Membership - Mutual respect, self-interest, understanding, and trust</li>
<li>Process/Structure - Members feel ownership — share stake in both process and outcome</li>
<li>Every level in each organization in collaborating groups participates in decision-making</li>
<li>Flexibility of collaborating group</li>
<li>Clarity of roles and guidelines</li>
<li>Communication - Open and frequent interaction, information, and discussion; Informal and formal channels of communications</li>
<li>Purpose - Goals clear and realistic to all partners; Shared vision;</li>
<li>Resources - Sufficient funds; Skilled convener</li>
</ul>
<p>Communicable Diseases</p>
<p>Goal: Understand the concepts of communicable and non-communicable disease</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Discuss communicable diseases in relation to their causation, prevention and control</li>
<li>Discuss prevention and treatment of non-communicable disease</li>
</ul>
<p>What are communicable diseases?</p>
<ul>
<li>A communicable disease such as a cold is a disease that spreads from person to person. Its also known as infectious or contagious</li>
<li>Communicable diseases are diseases that you can "catch" from someone or something else.</li>
<li>Some people may use the words contagious or infectious when talking about communicable diseases.</li>
<li>Communicable diseases spread from one person to another or from an animal to a person. The spread often happens via airborne viruses or bacteria, but also through blood or other bodily fluid.</li>
<li>Examples of communicable disease are:</li>
<li>HIV/AIDS</li>
<li>Influenza</li>
<li>Malaria</li>
<li>Polio</li>
<li>Tuberculosis</li>
<li>Hepatitis</li>
</ul>
<p>What do you "catch" when you get a communicable disease?</p>
<ul>
<li>When a person becomes sick with a communicable disease it means a germ has invaded their body.</li>
<li>Germs fear soap and water.</li>
<li>Washing your hands well and often is the best way to beat these tiny warriors.</li>
</ul>
<p>What are germs?</p>
<ul>
<li>Germs are tiny organisms (living things) that may cause disease. Germs are so small and sneaky that they creep into our body without being noticed. In fact, germs are so tiny that you need to use a microscope to see them. We don't know what hit us until we have symptoms (runny nose, cough, sore throat, fever, etc.)</li>
<li>Germs are microbes. A microbe is a tiny living organism that can only be seen with a microscope. Microbes are the smallest form of life on Earth. Although some microbes can make you sick or may even kill you, most are harmless, and some are extremely helpful. Microbes can be found virtually anywhere - in air, water, plants, animals and humans. A Germ is a microorganism that causes disease. Germs are also known as pathogens.</li>
<li>Broad example of germs are:</li>
<li>Bacteria – are everywhere. They live in sub-freezing cold temperatures and boiling hot temperatures. They live up high in the sky and down deep below the ocean. In fact scientists have found colonies of bacteria thriving 1,600 feet below sea level without oxygen or sunlight. Scientists also think there are signs of microbial life on Mars! Some bacteria are harmful but most are harmless or even helpful.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Viruses – depend upon a host to survive, grow, and reproduce. A host is the plant or animal on which or in which another organism lives. Viruses can't live outside of other living cells. Once they are inside the body, viruses can spread and make people sick. They reproduce by injecting their genes into a cell to produce thousands of new viruses. Viruses cause chicken pox, measles, flu, and many other diseases.
&gt; Fungi - are multi-celled plant-like organisms. Unlike other plants, fungi aren't able to produce their own food from soil, water, and air. Instead, fungi get their nutrition from plants, food, and animals. Fungi thrive in warm, damp environments. Most fungi are not dangerous. An example of something caused by fungi is athlete's foot - that itchy rash that teens and adults sometimes get between their toes.
&gt; Protozoa - are one-celled organisms like bacteria. Protozoa also love moisture and often spread diseases through contaminated water. Some protozoa cause intestinal infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disease-outbreak">Disease outbreak<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease-outbreak" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A disease outbreak is the occurrence of cases of disease in excess of what would normally be expected in a defined community, geographical area or season. An outbreak may occur in a restricted geographical area, or may extend over several countries. It may last for a few days or weeks, or for several years. All disease outbreaks must be investigated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember-all-microbes-are-not-germs">REMEMBER - ALL microbes are NOT Germs!<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember-all-microbes-are-not-germs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>We could not digest our food without microbes.</li>
<li>Garbage would not decay without microbes.</li>
<li>Plants would not grow without microbes.</li>
<li>The gas we pass is caused by bacteria in our intestines.</li>
<li>Without microbes there would be no life on earth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidemiologic-triangle-model-of-disease-causation">Epidemiologic triangle model of disease causation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidemiologic-triangle-model-of-disease-causation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The epidemiologic triangle or triad is the traditional model of infectious disease causation</li>
<li>It has 3 components:</li>
<li>External agent</li>
<li>Susceptible host</li>
<li>Environment that brings the host and agent together</li>
<li>Environment influences the agent, the host and the route of transmission of the agent from a source to the host</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-0db26a63.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-57ba5a40.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="agent-factors">Agent factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#agent-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Originally refers to an infectious microorganism – virus, bacterium, parasite, or other microbe</li>
<li>These agents must be present for a disease to occur. That is, they are necessary but not sufficient to cause a disease</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="host-factors">Host factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#host-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Are intrinsic factors that influence individual’s exposure, susceptibility, or response to a causative agent</li>
<li>Age, race, sex, socio-economic status and behaviors (smoking, drug abuse, lifestyle, sexual practices and contraception, eating habits) are some of the many host factors which affect a person’s likelihood of exposure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="environmental-factors">Environmental factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Are extrinsic factors which affect the agent and the opportunity for exposure</li>
<li>It includes physical factors such as geology, climate, physical surrounding, biological factors such as insects that transmit agents, socio-economic factors such as crowding, sanitation etc.</li>
<li>Agents, host and environmental factors interrelate in a variety of complex ways to produce a disease in humans.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="transmission-cycle">Transmission cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chain-of-infection">Chain of infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chain-of-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Transmission occurs when the agent leaves its reservoir or host through a portal of exit, and is conveyed by some mode of transmission, and enters through an appropriate portal of entry to infect a susceptible host.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reservoir">Reservoir<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reservoir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reservoir of an agent is the habitat in which an infectious agent normally lives, grows and multiplies</li>
<li>This includes humans, animals and the environment</li>
<li>The reservoir may or may not be the source from which an agent is transferred to a host</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-830dc5c8.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="human-reservoir">Human reservoir<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-reservoir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many of the common infectious diseases have human reservoirs.</li>
<li>Disease that are transmitted from person to person without intermediaries include sexually transmitted diseases, measles, mumps, streptococcal infections, most respiratory pathogens etc.</li>
<li>Smallpox was eradicated after the last human case was identified and isolated because humans were the only reservoir for the smallpox virus</li>
<li>Two types of human reservoir are:</li>
<li>Persons with symptomatic illness - Symptomatic persons are usually less likely to transmit infection widely because their symptoms increases their likelihood of being diagnosed and treated</li>
<li>Carriers - A carrier is a person without apparent disease who is nonetheless capable of transmitting the agents to others. Carriers may be asymptomatic carriers, who never show symptoms during the time they are infected, or may be incubatory or convalescent carriers who are capable of transmission before or after they are clinically ill</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="animal-reservoir">Animal reservoir<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#animal-reservoir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infectious diseases that are transmittable under normal conditions from animal to humans are called zoonoses. Such disease include brucellosis (cows and pigs), anthrax (sheep), plague (rodents), rabies (bats, dogs)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environmental-reservoir">Environmental reservoir<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-reservoir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Plants, soil and water are also reservoir for some infectious disease. Many fungal agents such as those causing histoplasmosis live and multiply in the soil</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="portal-of-exit-and-entry">Portal of exit and entry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#portal-of-exit-and-entry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the path by which an agent leaves the source host or enters</li>
<li>Tubercle bacilli and influenza viruses exit the respiratory tract; schistosome through urine; cholera vibrios through feces etc</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="modes-of-transmission">Modes of transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#modes-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>After an agent exists its natural reservoir, it may be transmitted to a susceptible host in numerous ways. These modes of transmission are classified as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Direct (Direct contact and direct spread) - There is immediate transfer of the agent from a reservoir to a susceptible host by direct contact or droplet spread. It occurs through kissing, skin-to-skin contact. Also refer to contact with soil or vegetation harboring infectious organisms</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indirect (Airborne, Vehicle borne, Vector borne) – This can be mechanical or biologic. An agent is carried from a reservoir (a susceptible host) by suspended air particles or by animate (vector) or inanimate (vehicle) intermediaries. Most vectors are arthropods such as mosquitoes, fleas and ticks. This is in contrast of instances in which an agent undergoes part of its life cycle inside a vector before being transmitted to a new host. When the agent undergoes changes within the vector, the vector is serving as both intermediate host and a mode of transmission. This type of direct transmission is called a biologic transmission</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vehicles that may directly transmit an agent include food, water, blood, handkerchiefs, bedding etc</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-managing-communicable-diseases-investigation-and-control-of-epidemics">Principles of managing communicable diseases (Investigation and control of epidemics)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-managing-communicable-diseases-investigation-and-control-of-epidemics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Health departments investigate suspected outbreaks for various reasons:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Need to institute control and prevention measures</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Opportunity for research and training</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Program considerations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Public relations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Political concern</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Legal obligations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Principles are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Outbreak occurs in any community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Outbreaks commonly occur in poor communities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It adds to burden of poverty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevention occurrences of outbreak is important</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spread of outbreak should be limited</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduce harm of outbreaks to individual</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Management of outbreak in competent way</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Stop the victim from injury of the outbreak
○ Break the chain of infection</p>
<ul>
<li>Steps of outbreak investigation:
○ Prepare for fieldwork – Prepare before leaving for the field. Preparation can be grouped into 3 categories:</li>
<li>Investigation – have scientific knowledge, supplies and equipment for investigation, review literature</li>
<li>Administration – pay attention to administrative procedures e.g. get approvals</li>
<li>Consultation – know your role in the field. Consult with local staff/people</li>
</ul>
<p>○ Establish the existence of an outbreak</p>
<ul>
<li>an outbreak or epidemic is the occurrence of more cases of disease than expected in a given area over a particular period of time</li>
<li>you can establish outbreak through regular analysis of data or report from health care providers</li>
<li>compare observed with expected cases</li>
</ul>
<p>○ Verify the diagnosis</p>
<ul>
<li>Establish what disease is occurring by proper diagnosis</li>
<li>Review clinical findings and laboratory results</li>
<li>Visit and talk to some patients to get better understanding of the clinical features</li>
</ul>
<p>○ Define and identify cases</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Establish a case definition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A case definition is a standard set of criteria for deciding whether an individual should be classified as having the health condition of interest</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Classify case definitions as: definite case; probable case; possible case</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Identify and count cases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cases that prompt concern are often only a small and no representative fraction of the total number of cases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask case patients if they know anyone else with the same illness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Collect the following information about every case:
○ Identifying information
○ Demographic information
○ Clinical information
○ Risk factor information
○ Reporter information</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>○ Perform descriptive epidemiology - Characterizing an outbreak by variables such as time, place and person is called descriptive epidemiology. Develop hypothesis. Evaluate hypothesis by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Use analytical epidemiology to test your hypothesis</li>
<li>You can also use case control</li>
<li>As necessary, reconsider/refine hypothesis and execute additional studies</li>
</ul>
<p>○ Implement control and prevention measures
○ Document and communicate findings through oral briefs or written report</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-control-and-eradication-of-diseases">Methods of control and eradication of diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-control-and-eradication-of-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There is an important distinction among the 3 terms, prevention, control, and eradication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Control: The reduction of disease incidence, prevalence, morbidity or mortality to a locally acceptable level as a result of deliberate efforts; continued intervention measures are required to maintain the reduction. Example: diarrheal diseases.</li>
<li>Elimination of infections: Reduction to zero of the incidence of infection caused by a specific agent in a defined geographical area as a result of deliberate efforts; continued measures to prevent re-establishment of transmission are required. Example: measles, poliomyelitis.</li>
<li>Eradication: Permanent reduction to zero of the worldwide incidence of infection caused by a specific agent as a result of deliberate efforts; intervention measures are no longer needed. Example: smallpox.</li>
<li>Extinction: The specific infectious agent no longer exists in nature or in the laboratory. Example: none.</li>
</ul>
<p>Figure2</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-dd831d29.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non">non<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>communicable disease</p>
<ul>
<li>These are</li>
</ul>
<p>medical conditions of noninfectious or non-transmittable to another person. Currently, the NCD are the leading causes of death and disease burden worldwide</p>
<ul>
<li>The 4 main types of non-communicable diseases are cardiovascular diseases (like heart attacks and stroke), cancers, chronic respiratory diseases (such as chronic obstructed pulmonary disease and asthma) and diabetes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>All age groups and all regions are affected by NCDs. NCDs are often associated with older age groups, but evidence shows that 16 million of all deaths attributed to non-communicable diseases occur before the age of 70. Of these "premature" deaths, 82% occurred in low- and middle-income countries. Children, adults</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>and the elderly are all vulnerable to the risk factors that contribute to non-communicable diseases, whether from unhealthy diets, physical inactivity, exposure to tobacco smoke or the effects of the harmful use of alcohol.</p>
<p>These diseases are driven by forces that include ageing, rapid unplanned urbanization, and the globalization of unhealthy lifestyles. For example, globalization of unhealthy lifestyles like unhealthy diets may show up in individuals as raised blood pressure, increased blood glucose, elevated blood lipids, and obesity. These are called 'intermediate risk factors' which can lead to cardiovascular disease, a NCD.</p>
<p>A risk factor is any attribute, characteristic or exposure of an individual that increases the likelihood of developing a disease or injury. The following are risk factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Modifiable behavioral risk factors - Tobacco use, physical inactivity, unhealthy diet and the harmful use of alcohol increase the risk of NCDs.</li>
<li>Metabolic/physiological risk factors - These behaviors lead to four key metabolic/physiological changes that increase the risk of NCDs: Raised blood pressure, Overweight/obesity, Hyperglycemia (high blood glucose levels) and Hyperlipidemia (high levels of fat in the blood).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-classification">Risks classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>High risk includes any of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Percutaneous (e.g., needle stick) or mucous membrane exposure to blood or body fluids of a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
<li>Exposure to the blood or body fluids (including but not limited to feces, saliva, sweat, urine, vomit, and semen) of a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic without appropriate personal protective equipment (PPE)</li>
<li>Processing blood or body fluids of a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic without appropriate PPE or standard biosafety precautions</li>
<li>Direct contact with a dead body without appropriate PPE in a country with widespread transmission or cases in urban areas with uncertain control measures.</li>
<li>Having lived in the immediate household and provided direct care to a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="some-risk-includes-any-of-the-following">Some risk includes any of the following:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#some-risk-includes-any-of-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In countries with widespread transmission or cases in urban areas with uncertain control measures:</li>
<li>direct contact while using appropriate PPE with a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic or with the person's body fluids</li>
<li>any direct patient care in other healthcare settings</li>
<li>Close contact in households, healthcare facilities, or community settings with a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
<li>Close contact is defined as being for a prolonged period of time while not wearing appropriate PPE within approximately 3 feet (1 meter) of a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="low-but-not-zero-risk-includes-any-of-the-following">Low (but not zero) risk includes any of the following:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#low-but-not-zero-risk-includes-any-of-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Having been in a country with widespread transmission or cases in urban areas with uncertain control measures within the past 21 days and having had no known exposures</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Having brief direct contact (e.g., shaking hands) while not wearing appropriate PPE, with a person with Ebola while the person was in the early stage of disease</li>
<li>Brief proximity, such as being in the same room for a brief period of time, with a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
<li>In countries without widespread transmission or cases in urban settings with uncertain control measures: direct contact while using appropriate PPE with a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic or with the person's body fluids</li>
<li>Traveled on an aircraft with a person with Ebola while the person was symptomatic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="no-identifiable-risk-includes">No identifiable risk includes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#no-identifiable-risk-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Contact with an asymptomatic person who had contact with person with Ebola</li>
<li>Contact with a person with Ebola before the person developed symptoms</li>
<li>Having been more than 21 days previously in a country with widespread transmission or cases in urban areas with uncertain control measures</li>
<li>Having been in a country with Ebola cases, but without widespread transmission or cases in urban settings with uncertain control measures, and not having any other exposures as defined above</li>
<li>Having remained on or in the immediate vicinity of an aircraft or ship during the entire time that the conveyance was present in a country with widespread transmission or cases in urban areas with uncertain control measures, and having had no direct contact with anyone from the community.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control-strategies">Prevention and control strategies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control-strategies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A comprehensive approach is needed that requires all sectors, including health, finance, foreign affairs, education, agriculture, planning and others, to work together to reduce the risks associated with NCDs, as well as promote the interventions to prevent and control them.</li>
<li>To focus on lessening the risk factors associated with these diseases. Low-cost solutions exist to reduce the common modifiable risk factors (mainly tobacco use, unhealthy diet and physical inactivity, and the harmful use of alcohol) and map the epidemic of NCDs and their risk factors.</li>
<li>High impact essential NCD interventions that can be delivered through a primary health-care approach to strengthen early detection and timely treatment. These measures can be implemented in various resource levels.</li>
<li>Lower-income countries generally have lower capacity for the prevention and control of non-communicable diseases. Countries with inadequate health insurance coverage are unlikely to provide universal access to essential NCD interventions.</li>
<li>Prevention is NCD is in three levels:</li>
<li>Primary prevention - is aimed at maintaining a healthy population; i.e., preventing the occurrence of disease. It involves the healthy population.</li>
<li>Secondary prevention - (also called disease control) attempts to minimize resultant damage after disease has occurred and primary prevention has failed.</li>
<li>Tertiary prevention - consists of rehabilitation after primary and secondary prevention has failed.</li>
<li>Secondary and tertiary Prevention is aimed at the diseased or patient population.</li>
<li>Preventive approaches are:</li>
<li>Naturalizing the reservoir</li>
<li>Reducing contact potential</li>
<li>Increasing resistance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="socioeconomic-impacts-of-ncds">Socioeconomic impacts of NCDs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#socioeconomic-impacts-of-ncds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>NCDs threaten progress towards the UN Millennium Development Goals and post-2015 development agenda.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Poverty is closely linked with NCDs. The rapid rise in NCDs is predicted to impede poverty reduction initiatives in low-income countries, particularly by increasing household costs associated with health care.</li>
<li>Vulnerable and socially disadvantaged people get sicker and die sooner than people of higher social positions, especially because they are at greater risk of being exposed to harmful products, such as tobacco or unhealthy food, and have limited access to health services.</li>
<li>In low-resource settings, health-care costs for cardiovascular diseases, cancers, diabetes or chronic lung diseases can quickly drain household resources, driving families into poverty. The exorbitant costs of NCDs, including often lengthy and expensive treatment and loss of breadwinners, are forcing millions of people into poverty annually, stifling development.</li>
<li>In many countries, harmful drinking and unhealthy diet and lifestyles occur both in higher and lower income groups. However, high-income groups can access services and products that protect them from the greatest risks while lower-income groups can often not afford such products and services.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-treatment">Basic treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Common</strong> - There are numerous common communicable diseases, such as throat colds and the flu. They often produce symptoms like sore throat, runny nose, coughing, sneezing, headache, fever and nausea. These can typically be treated with adequate rest and over-the-counter medication. Medication for common communicable diseases may include pain relievers like Tylenol as well as nasal decongestants, cough syrups, anti-nausea pills and throat drops. Common communicable diseases usually dissipate over the course of a few days or weeks.</p>
<p><strong>Chronic</strong> - Chronic communicable diseases are severe and not usually spread from person to person via airborne pathogens. They may be spread via parasites, sexual contact or transmission of bodily fluids like blood. Unlike throat colds or other common illnesses, chronic communicable diseases may last months or even a lifetime. Examples of chronic communicable disease include malaria, Lyme disease, diphtheria and hepatitis. Treatment for chronic communicable diseases usually involves some form of hospitalization, intravenous antibiotics, prescription medication and intensive care.</p>
<p><strong>Vaccines</strong> - One effective way to treat a communicable disease is by receiving a vaccine before your body becomes infected. Vaccines work by infecting your body with a weakened strain of the actual disease. Your body then produces antibodies to fight the disease. Antibodies remain in the system after the weakened strain is gone and protect the body from later infections. Certain vaccines need only to be administered once, such as vaccines for mumps, measles, whooping cough and polio. Others, like the flu vaccine, should be taken annually.</p>
<p><strong>Prevention/Solution</strong> - Prevention is the most effective form of treatment for communicable disease. Boost your immune system by incorporating high levels of antioxidants, fruits, vegetables and antihistamines into your diet. Engage in at least 30 minutes of exercise daily to maintain strength and proper circulation. Drink high amounts of water (in excess of two liters per day) and maintain adequate rest for your body. Wash your hands with soap and water after using the bathroom, handling uncooked meat, sneezing, coughing or touching a dirty surface.</p>
<p><strong>Warning</strong> - Some communicable diseases have no cure. For example, there is no cure for sexually transmitted diseases (STDs) like herpes and HIV. Avoiding sexual contact with individuals infected with STDs is the best and only way to ensure that you do not become infected with such communicable diseases</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-participation-in-disease-control-program">Community participation in disease control program<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-participation-in-disease-control-program" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The determinants of community participation in disease control are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Political background,</li>
<li>Community characteristics,</li>
<li>Managerial capacity of the provider</li>
<li>Epidemiology of the disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>Recently, community participation in organized efforts to control Chagas' disease has become more dynamic, with increasingly active involvement by local community members.</p>
<p>Community participation per se has inherent value because of its positive effect on social relationships and community solidarity.</p>
<p>*** Outline evidence based community participation in the control of communicable disease***</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disease-prevention-control-and-eradication">Disease Prevention, control and eradication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease-prevention-control-and-eradication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Improve knowledge and skills on disease prevention</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the purposes and levels of disease prevention</li>
<li>Explain the approaches and challenges to disease prevention</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevention – is defined as intervention or interventions that interrupt the web of causality leading to one or more aspects of ill health.</p>
<p>Preventive healthcare – these are measures taken for disease prevention, as opposed to disease treatment. It is also called preventive medicine or prophylaxis. Each year, millions of people die preventable deaths.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purpose-of-disease-prevention">Purpose of disease prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-disease-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevention is better than cure</li>
<li>Stop new cases of disease from occurring</li>
<li>Stop existing cases of diseases from spreading</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-level-prevention">Primary level prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-level-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Here the goal is to protect healthy people from developing a disease or experiencing an injury in the first place. For example:</li>
<li>education about good nutrition, the importance of regular exercise, and the dangers of tobacco, alcohol and other drugs</li>
<li>education and legislation about proper seatbelt and helmet use</li>
<li>regular exams and screening tests to monitor risk factors for illness</li>
<li>immunization against infectious disease</li>
<li>controlling potential hazards at home and in the workplace</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-level-prevention">Secondary level prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-level-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These interventions happen after an illness or serious risk factors have already been diagnosed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The goal is to halt or slow the progress of disease (if possible) in its earliest stages; in the case of injury, goals include limiting long-term disability and preventing re-injury. For example:</li>
<li>telling people to take daily, low-dose aspirin to prevent a first or second heart attack or stroke</li>
<li>recommending regular exams and screening tests in people with known risk factors for illness</li>
<li>providing suitably modified work for injured workers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tertiary-level-prevention">Tertiary level prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tertiary-level-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This focuses on helping people manage complicated, long-term health problems such as diabetes, heart disease, cancer and chronic musculoskeletal pain.</li>
<li>The goals include preventing further physical deterioration and maximizing quality of life. For example:</li>
<li>cardiac or stroke rehabilitation programs</li>
<li>chronic pain management programs</li>
<li>patient support groups</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-techniques">Preventive techniques<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-techniques" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevention is the first line of defense against disease.</li>
<li>At least 8 preventive techniques are available for disease prevention:</li>
<li>✓ Exclusion - of causative agents of disease from specific geographic areas, or quarantine.</li>
<li>✓ Control methods - such as immunization, environmental control, and chemical agents to protect specific animal populations from endemic diseases, diseases normally present in an area.</li>
<li>✓ The mass education - of people about disease prevention.</li>
<li>✓ Early diagnosis - of illness among members of an animal population is important so that disease manifestations do not become too severe and so that affected animals can be more easily managed and treated.</li>
<li>✓ Recognition - of the relationship among high risk population</li>
<li>✓ Health protection measures - and the second group is the health promotion measures. The two approaches are complementary and interactive, and it is unlikely that one would be effective without the other. A third group of measures include preventive health services.</li>
<li>✓ Health promotion measures - include activities that individuals and communities can use to promote healthy life style. For example: public education programs, health warning labels, advertising and marketing, and media portrayals.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="simple-things-you-can-do-to-prevent-illness">Simple things you can do to prevent illness.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#simple-things-you-can-do-to-prevent-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep Immunizations up to date</li>
<li>Wash your hands often</li>
<li>Be aware of what you eat, and be careful how you prepare it</li>
<li>Use antibiotics exactly as prescribed</li>
<li>Report to your doctor any worsening infection that does not get better after you take a prescribed antibiotic</li>
<li>Be cautious around wild and domestic animals that are not familiar to you</li>
<li>Avoid areas of insect infestation</li>
<li>Avoid unsafe unprotected sex and injection drug use</li>
<li>Stay alert to disease threats when you travel</li>
<li>When sick, allow yourself time to heal and recover.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The strategic directions to disease prevention</p>
<ul>
<li>The strategic directions provide a strong foundation for all of our nation’s prevention efforts and include core recommendations necessary to build a prevention-based strategy.</li>
<li>Each Strategic Direction guides actions that will demonstrably improve health. Together, the Strategic Directions create the web needed to fully support in leading longer and healthier lives.</li>
<li>The four Strategic Directions are:</li>
<li>Healthy and Safe Community Environments</li>
<li>Clinical and Community Preventive Services</li>
<li>Empowered People</li>
<li>Elimination of Health Disparities</li>
<li>Within the Strategy, the priorities provide evidenced-based recommendations that are most likely to reduce the burden of the leading causes of preventable death and major illness.</li>
<li>The Priorities are designed to improve health and wellness of the population, including those groups disproportionately affected by disease and injury.</li>
<li>The seven Priorities are:</li>
<li>Tobacco Free Living</li>
<li>Preventing Drug Abuse and Excessive Alcohol Use</li>
<li>Healthy Eating</li>
<li>Active Living</li>
