<li>Injury and Violence Free Living</li>
<li>Reproductive and Sexual Health</li>
<li>Mental and Emotional Well-Being</li>
</ul>
<p>A Plan for Better Health and Wellness</p>
<p>The overarching goal of the National Prevention Strategy is to increase the number of people who are healthy at every stage of life. The strategy provides evidence-based recommendations that are fundamental to improving the nation's health through the active engagement of all sectors of society to help achieve four broad strategic directions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Building Healthy and Safe Community Environments - Prevention of disease starts in our communities and at home; not just in the doctor's office. For example, businesses and employers can adopt practices to encourage their workforce to increase physical activity and reduce pollution (e.g., workplace flexibility, rideshare and vanpool programs, park-and-ride incentives, travel demand management initiatives, and telecommuting options).</li>
<li>Expanding Quality Preventive Services in Both Clinical and Community Settings - When people receive preventive care, such as immunizations and cancer screenings, they have better health and lower health care costs. For example, expanding the linkages between clinical and community prevention efforts, such as diabetes prevention programs that support preventive efforts among underserved groups and can improve access to preventive services.</li>
<li>Empowering People to Make Healthy Choices - Policies and programs can make healthy options the easy and affordable choice, and when people have access to actionable and easy-to-understand information and resources, they are empowered to make healthier choices. For example, health care professionals can use multiple communication tools (e.g., mobile phone applications, personal health records, and credible health websites) and culturally competent methods to support more traditional written and oral communication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Eliminating Health Disparities - By eliminating disparities in achieving and maintaining health, we can help improve quality of life for all Americans. For example, health care providers can train and hire more qualified staff from underrepresented racial and ethnic minority groups and people with disabilities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-environment-and-individual-approaches-to-disease-prevention">Role of environment and individual approaches to disease prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-environment-and-individual-approaches-to-disease-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ecosystem – Environment is where man, pathogens (virus, bacteria, fungi and protozoa) live. The interaction between man with environment enable transfer of germs to human system</li>
<li>Difficulties in changing behavior - To prevent disease we increasingly ask people to begin do things that they have not done previously, to stop doing things that they have been doing for years and to do more of some things and less of others</li>
<li>Pattern of disease rate - Some groups often have a characteristic over time even though individuals come and go from these groups. If groups have different rates over time, there may be something promotes or discourages disease among individuals in those groups</li>
<li>Socio-economic status - A consistent finding dated from the twelfth century, is that people in the lowest socioeconomic groups have the highest rates of morbidity and mortality, whether the socioeconomic status was studied in relation to education, income, or occupation: the lower the level the higher the death and morbidity rate.</li>
<li>Marital status - It has been known for many years that people who are not married-whether single, separated, widowed or divorced- have higher mortality rates than married people.</li>
<li>Gender - One of the most well-established facts among students of health and disease is that men have higher mortality rates than women. This excess of male deaths occurs at every age and for every major cause for which comparison is possible.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-education">Health education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Is any is any combination of learning experiences designed to help individuals and communities improve their health, by increasing their knowledge or influencing their attitudes.</li>
<li>A level of education plays a major role in health education. Different levels of education has different levels of perception and understanding</li>
<li>Target audiences are those that the education is intended for. They can be:</li>
<li>Primary target audience – people who are directly affected</li>
<li>Secondary target audience – people who are indirectly affected</li>
<li>Tertiary target audience – people who are indirectly affected and can influence policy</li>
<li>Some of the education outlets in the community include chief's baraza, churches, schools, social places, boda-boda terminals etc.</li>
<li>Promoting health and preventing disease in the population and in the wider community involves the following:</li>
<li>Demonstrate effective, patient-centered counseling</li>
<li>Interventions that address patients' personal health behaviors and practices are vitally important.</li>
<li>Clinicians can help individuals change their health-related behaviors by using efficient, patient-centered counseling strategies that are based on an understanding of how people change.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Understand the principles of and procedures for screening.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Another central health promotion/disease prevention strategy that students need to be skilled in is screening, or testing for health problems in the absence of symptoms or signs indicating the presence of such a problem.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students need to learn (1) when screening is appropriate, (2) what procedures to use and how to use them effectively, and (3) how to interpret and use the results of screening tests.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the importance and use of immunization and prophylaxis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Understand the important role that widespread childhood immunization has played in drastically reducing the incidence of many illnesses, including diphtheria, pertussis, tetanus, poliomyelitis, measles, mumps, and rubella.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In addition, learn which childhood immunizations are essential, when and how to administer them, and potential risks.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Knowledge of the appropriate use of adult immunizations is also necessary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Implement strategies to promote the health of the population.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Although health care professionals traditionally have focused on individual patients who present themselves for care one at a time in the office or clinic, students preparing for practice in today's health care system also must learn to focus on the care of populations of patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Engage in public education and advocacy to prevent disease.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For some health problems, preventive interventions aimed at the wider community may be especially appropriate and effective.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Such problems include unintended pregnancy in adolescents, youth violence, and domestic violence, initiation of tobacco use, sexually transmitted diseases, healthy dietary practices, and unintentional injuries.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-challenges-to-disease-prevention">The challenges to disease prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-challenges-to-disease-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="political-challenges">Political challenges<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#political-challenges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The scope for the prevention of diseases is enormous.</li>
<li>There will be scope for prevention of all types and at all levels, and much of this will require political change.</li>
<li>Smoking-related diseases are increasing in developing countries where tobacco companies have been promoting sales.</li>
<li>Widespread disease and death still occur in many countries which don't have a clean and plentiful water supply.</li>
<li>Wars and armed conflict have hindered or destroyed the development of basic infrastructure in many parts of the world. Worldwide, it is evident that measures at government level will yield the greatest gains.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-challenges">Specific challenges<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-challenges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Many of these are clinical or individual challenges.</li>
<li>This may include the barriers to prevention. Articles of particular note include:</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="taxation-and-cost-issues">Taxation and cost issues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#taxation-and-cost-issues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Consumption may fall so much that total revenue from that source falls. This can be politically challenging with industry concerned about economic damage.</li>
<li>Most interventions have costs and do not have the advantages of revenue generation associated with, for example, taxation on tobacco. This includes screening programmes or advertising campaigns.</li>
<li>Immunization programmes cost money to set up in private health institutions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="demographic-issues">Demographic issues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demographic-issues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A growing elderly population puts more strain on health and social services. A significant number of people now spend a quarter of their lives as pensioners retired from working life.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personal-barriers">Personal barriers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cost and quality</li>
<li>Information</li>
<li>Exercise</li>
<li>Social, educational and cultural barriers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="administrative-barriers">Administrative barriers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administrative-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-diagnosis">Community Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Improve skills and knowledge on community diagnosis</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define the concepts of community diagnosis and its purposes</li>
<li>Describe the steps in carrying out community diagnosis</li>
<li>Conduct a participatory rural appraisal as a tool for community diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<p>Community – is a cluster of people with at least one common characteristic (geographic location, occupation, ethnicity, housing condition). It can also be defined as a group of people with a common characteristic or interest living together within a larger society</p>
<p>Diagnosis – is the identification and confirmation of a problem</p>
<p>Community sub systems - A community is a whole entity that functions because of the interdependence of its parts or subsystems. Community core are: history, socio-demographic characteristics, vital statistics, values/beliefs/religions. Community sub systems are: Physical environment; Education; Safety and transportation; Politics and government; Health and social services; Communication; Economics; and Recreation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-diagnosis">Community diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Refers to the identification and quantification of health problems in a community as a whole in terms of mortality and morbidity rates and ratios, and identification of their correlates for the purpose of defining those at risk or those in need of health care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is a comprehensive assessment of health status of the community in relation to its social, physical and biological environment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>According to WHO definition, it is “a quantitative and qualitative description of the health of citizens and the factors which influence their health. It identifies problems, proposes areas for improvement and stimulates action</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Purpose - The purpose of community diagnosis is to define existing problems, determine available resources and set priorities for planning, implementing and evaluating health action, by and for the community. The following are the importance of community diagnosis:</p>
<ul>
<li>Analyze the health status of the community</li>
<li>Evaluate the health resources, services, and systems of care within the community</li>
<li>Assess attitudes toward community health services and issues</li>
<li>Identify priorities, establish goals, and determine courses of action to improve the health status of the community</li>
<li>Establish an epidemiologic baseline for measuring improvement over time.</li>
<li>To act as a data reference</li>
<li>To provide an overall picture of the local community and the residents’ concerns</li>
<li>To suggest priority areas for intervention and the feasible solutions</li>
<li>To indicate the resource allocation and the direction of work plans</li>
<li>It helps to find the common problems or diseases, which are troublesome to the people and are easily preventable in the community.</li>
<li>It is a tool to disclose the hidden problems that are not visible to the community people but are being affected by them.</li>
<li>It helps to access the group of underprivileged people who are unable to use the available facilities due to poverty, prevailing discriminations or other reasons.</li>
<li>It helps to find the real problems of the community people which might not have perceived by them as problems.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implementation-framework-and-process">Implementation framework and process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implementation-framework-and-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-a3bc473d.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-information-in-community-diagnosis-and-intervention-sources">Types of information in community diagnosis and intervention sources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-information-in-community-diagnosis-and-intervention-sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The information collected in a community diagnosis is called health indicators</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Characteristics of indicators:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Valid, i.e., they should actually measure what they are supposed to measure;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reliable and objective, i.e., the answers should be the same if measured by different people in similar circumstances;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sensitive, i.e., they should be sensitive to changes in the situation concerned,</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Specific, i.e., they should reflect changes only in the situation concerned,
Feasible, i.e., they should have the ability to obtain data needed, and;
Relevant, i.e., they should contribute to the understanding of the phenomenon of interest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classifications-of-indicators">Classifications of indicators:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classifications-of-indicators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mortality indicators; Morbidity indicators; Disability rates; Nutritional status indicators; Health care delivery indicators; Utilization rates; Indicators of social and mental health; Environmental indicators; Socio-economic indicators; Health policy indicators; Indicators of quality of life' Other indicators</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Mortality indicators are: ○ Crude death rates ○ Specific death rates: age/disease ○ Expectation of life ○ Infant mortality rate ○ Maternal mortality rate ○ Proportionate mortality ratio ○ Case Fatality rate</th><th>Morbidity indicators are: ○ Incidence and prevalence ○ Notification rates ○ Attendance rates: out-patient clinics or health centers. ○ Admission and discharge rates ○ Hospital stay duration rates</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Disability indicators are: ○ No. of days of restricted activity ○ Bed disability days ○ Work/School loss days within a specified period. ○ Expectation of life free of disability</td><td>Nutritional indicators are: ○ Anthropometrics measurements ○ Height of children at school entry ○ Prevalence of low birth weight ○ Clinical surveys: Anaemia, Hypothyroidism, Night blindness</td></tr><tr><td>Health care delivery indicators are: ○ Doctor / Population ratio ○ Doctor / Nurse ratio ○ Population / Bed ratio ○ Population / per health center</td><td>Utilization indicators are: ○ Proportion of infants who are fully immunized in the 1styear of life i.e..immunization coverage. ○ Proportion of pregnant women who receive ANC. ○ Hospital-Beds occupancy rate. ○ Hospital-Beds turn-over ratio</td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr><tr><td>Social/mental health indicators are: ○ Suicide &amp; Homicide rates ○ Road traffic accidents ○ Alcohol and drug abuse</td><td>Environmental health indicators are: ○ Measures of Pollution ○ The proportion of people having access to safe water and sanitation facilities ○ Vectors density</td></tr><tr><td>Socio-economic indicators are: ○ Rate of population increase ○ Per capita income ○ Level of unemployment ○ Literacy rates - females ○ Family size ○ Housing condition e.g. No. of persons per room</td><td>Health policy indicators are: ○ Proportion of resources spent on health services. ○ Proportion of funds spent on health related activities. ○ Proportion of total health resources devoted to primary health care</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-diagnosis-process-steps">Community diagnosis process/steps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-diagnosis-process-steps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Implementation of community diagnosis takes stages:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Initiation stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Set up a dedicated committee or working group to manage and coordinate the project.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The committee should involve relevant parties such as government departments, health professionals and non-governmental organizations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Identify the available budget and resources to determine the scope of the diagnosis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some of the common areas (scope) to be studied may include health status, lifestyles, living conditions, socioeconomic conditions, physical and social infrastructure, inequalities, as well as public health services and policies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once the scope is defined, a working schedule to conduct the community diagnosis, production and dissemination of report should be set.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Data collection and analysis stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Collect both quantitative and qualitative data.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Population census and statistical data (e.g. population size, sex and age structure, medical services, public health, social services, education, housing, public security and transportation, etc.) can provide background of the district.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Collect community data by conducting surveys through self-administered questionnaires, face to face interviews, focus groups and telephone interviews.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In order to ensure reliability of the findings, an experienced organization such as an academic institute can be employed for conducting the study.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The sampling method should be carefully designed and the sample size should be large enough to provide sufficient data to draw reliable conclusions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analyze and interpret the data.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Here are some practical tips on data analysis and presentation:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>statistical information is best presented as rates or ratios for comparison</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>trends and projections are useful for monitoring changes over a time period for future planning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>local district data can be compared with other districts or the whole population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>graphical presentation is preferred for easy understanding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diagnosis stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diagnosis of the community is reached from conclusions drawn from the data analysis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It should preferably comprise three areas:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health status of the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Determinants of health in the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Potential for healthy community development</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dissemination stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The production of the community diagnosis report is not an end in itself</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Efforts should be put into communication to ensure that targeted actions are taken.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The target audience for the community diagnosis includes policy-makers, health professionals and the general public in the community.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The report can be disseminated through the following channels:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Presentations at meetings of the health boards and committees, or forums organized, local community groups and the general public</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Press release</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thematic events (such as health fairs and other health promotion programmes)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="evaluation-of-community-diagnosis">Evaluation of community diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-of-community-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is advisable to carry out evaluation after completing the community diagnosis.</li>
<li>The following are the importance of evaluating community diagnosis process:</li>
<li>Identification of what diagnostic approaches that worked best versus those never worked</li>
<li>It provides answers to the following questions: Did the diagnosis reveal the hidden problem in the community? Was the process interfered with by biasness? Were there missing responses in the questionnaires? Was the correct sample size used? What is the accuracy level of the responses? What can be improved in future diagnosis processes?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-community-based-research">Principles of community based research<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-community-based-research" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Community based research is a research that strives to be:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Community situated - begins with a research topic of practical relevance to the community (as opposed to individual scholars) and is carried out in community settings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Collaborative - community members and researchers equitably share control of the research agenda through active and reciprocal involvement in the research design, implementation and dissemination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Action-oriented - the process and results are useful to community members in making positive social change and to promote social equity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The following are its principles:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Recognizes community as a unit of identity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Builds on strengths and resources within the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Facilitates collaborative partnerships in all phases of the research</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Integrates knowledge and action for the mutual benefit of all partners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Promotes a co-learning and empowering process that attends to social inequalities and different perspectives</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Disseminates findings and knowledge gains to all partners in an accessible way.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Involves long term commitment by all partners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The relevance of the research topic is identified or verified by community members.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The resources of research (financial, expertise, etc.) are shared with community members, particularly those most affected by the research topic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The research process recognizes and addresses power imbalances between researchers and community members.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The research process is driven by values, including: empowerment, supportive relationships, social change, learning as an ongoing process and respect for diversity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The research process and results are accessible and understandable to community members.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The research process and results consider and adapt to the context in which the research is conducted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The research leaves a legacy, both in terms of the utilization of research results, as well as in the future collaboration among partners.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="roles-of-households-and-communities">Roles of households and communities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#roles-of-households-and-communities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What are the roles of the following in community diagnosis? {Give as group work}</li>
<li>Individual; Family; Institutions; Faith based organization; Leaders</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="participatory-rural-appraisal">Participatory rural appraisal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#participatory-rural-appraisal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is a technique typically used in the field to gather qualitative data, often to complement quantitative data</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Its aims are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ To involve local people in the selection, design, planning and implementation of programmes and projects that will affect them</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Ensures that local perception, attitudes, values and knowledge are taken into account as fully as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ To make continuous and comprehensive feedback an integral part of all development activities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It acts as alternative to the two common qualitative methods:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Questionnaires which often proved lengthy, costly and prone to errors,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rushed site visits by researchers to collect haphazard data from local elites.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>PRA uses a combination of approaches and methods to enable rural people to share enhance and analyze their knowledge of life and conditions, to plan and to act.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Uses a range of methods to ensure reliability and validity, and to enable cross-checking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Facilitate rapid and progressive learning with and from rural people</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Enables vulnerable groups in a community to have a voice and impart their views on issues of transportation and access from which they are most often excluded.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Include: women, the elderly, disabled and even school children, researchers and other professionals are able to paint a realistic picture of community life; and through use of the different PRA techniques,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It answers the following questions relevant to community needs:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Which community members require the use of transport?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When is access required?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Why is access required?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where to local people travel to?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How is transportation paid for?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What modes of transport to people take?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>PRA methods are based on the following principles:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ A reversal of learning - to learn with and from rural people, directly, on the site, face to face, gaining from local, physical, technical and social knowledge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Learning rapidly and progressively - with flexible use of methods, improvisation, iteration, and cross-checking, being adaptable in a learning process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Seeking diversity - Looking for, noticing and investigating contradictions, anomalies and difference.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Triangulating – use of combined approaches for data collection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Facilitating by the local people - Facilitating, investigation, analysis, presentation and learning by rural people themselves, so that they present and own their own outcomes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Preparation - Ensure that all available secondary data on the locality and subject has been reviewed, allowing suitable villages to be identified to capture a broad sample, before surveying commences.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Facilitation - It is imperative that the external professional displays good facilitation skills, which aims to enable local people to undertake some or all of the investigation, mapping, modeling, diagramming, ranking, scoring, quantification, analysis, presentation and planning themselves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Behavior and attitudes - The behavior and attitudes of external facilitators are of primary importance, more important than methods even. All important attitudes include: critical self-awareness and embracing error, sitting down, listening and learning, not lecturing but allowing the villagers to be the main teachers and analysts.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Longevity - Participatory approaches are not substitutes for, but are rather an integral part of, long term dialogue and sustained interaction. A single, brief participatory exercise with a group of local people will not lead to positive and lasting change.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The following are methods of PRA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Triangulation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Triangulation is simply a method of linking different survey methods in order to crosscheck the information collected from each method.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Triangulation is of particular use when employing mapping, ranking and scoring, flow diagrams, Venn diagrams and wealth ranking techniques, as these involve group participation which may require some verification.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Prior to conducting any PRA techniques, researchers should be clear in their mind as to what exactly it is they are researching, and to have some realistic objectives of the PRA surveys.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Researchers should act on what they see, and recognize distinctions in gender, age, and wealth etc. amongst the community observation also aids improvisation, particularly when carrying out diagramming techniques, allowing household implements for example to be used in the PRA methods.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Semi-structured interviews</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Participatory methods have contributed to adjusting the interview to make it more conversational, while still controlled and structured.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> This is whereby only some of the questions and topics are predetermined, whilst the majority of questions will be formulated during the interview.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Questions are asked according to a flexible checklist and not from a formal questionnaire.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ranking and scoring techniques</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Ranking and scoring have long been used to assess people's expectations, beliefs, attitudes, preferences and opinions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Ranking and scoring means placing something in order:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ranking: putting in order</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scoring: weighting differences</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Matrix ranking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Matrices can be used to express other issues, where a two dimensional comparison is useful, such as where frequency or occurrence can be illustrated in the same way as preference scoring.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Matrix ranking involves listing the elements down one side, and the criteria on which they are judged, gained from informal discussion or pairwise ranking, across the top.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Each element is then considered in terms of each criterion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diagramming</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Diagrams, including maps, sketches and transects, summaries data in such a way that they can be used for different purposes such as planning, field discussion, and analysis and problem identification.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> They are useful for opening up discussions between community members and the external team and helping clarify issues and questions.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Participatory mapping</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Maps can be used to identify the comparative location and importance of different resources within an area.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ They can examine a great breadth of subject matter, and allow for a range of different types of map to be produced for one area or for comparative analysis by different groups within the same area.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Maps are also a useful tool to aid communication and to generate the following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide a framework for discussion over the relative location of resources</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Highlight resources of importance, using maps as a spatial guide</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Raise issues which affect or are affected by these resources</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analyze the present status or condition of a location</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Create a focus for interest in a discussion over resources</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social maps can be used to locate houses, services and infrastructure within an area.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maps should be used as a visual stimulant, to identify the parameters faced by local people and to facilitate discussion about the importance people place on infrastructure provision etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The following are constraints of PRA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The process of carrying out PRA methods requires mutual respect and trust between external facilitators and village participants; this takes time, and requires an understanding of the local culture.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Time consuming</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A common mistake is, projects do not contact local government officials from the start - hence no local government support which is a prerequisite for success.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The step from problem identification with participatory PRA methods to follow up project definition is often poorly prepared.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Project officers should leave any class and gender biases they may carry at home!</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The researcher must be able to listen but also to establish dialogue and share own experience.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural protocol may be difficult to follow</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It raises expectations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A researcher stays in the village throughout the training session</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-health-survey">Community Health Survey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Increase skills and knowledge on concepts and procedures of conducting community survey</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Understand the terms used in community health survey, reasons and types of survey</li>
<li>Describe the process of carrying a survey, biased sample and response rate in relation to survey</li>
<li>Outline points to note in constructing survey tool, causes of inaccuracy and report presentation</li>
<li>Describe evaluation and feedback in relation to community survey</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">Definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A survey - is defined as a brief interview or discussion with individuals about a specific topic</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Community survey - is a way of asking group or community members what they see as the most important needs of that group or community.</li>
<li>Questionnaire - is a research instrument consisting of a series of questions and other prompts for the purpose of gathering information from respondents.</li>
<li>Evaluation - is a systematic determination of a subject's merit, worth and significance, using criteria governed by a set of standards.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2eed8abe">Reasons – The following are reasons for carrying out a survey:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2eed8abe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Gather information about residents, their opinion, attitude and knowledge</li>
<li>Measuring behaviors and population characteristics</li>
<li>Solicit community reaction to policies, proposals and solutions</li>
<li>Residents assess effectiveness of program, facilities and services</li>
<li>Make residence aware of problems and their effects</li>
<li>Provide residence access to policy making process</li>
<li>Provide opportunity for communities to influence public decisions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="when-can-you-do-a-community-survey">When can you do a community survey?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-can-you-do-a-community-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When your group is just starting out</li>
<li>When there is doubt as to what the most important needs are</li>
<li>When your group members disagree on this point among themselves</li>
<li>When you need to convince outside funders or supporters that you are addressing the most important community problems</li>
<li>When the community asks you to do it</li>
<li>When you want to be sure that you will have community support for whatever you choose to do.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-each-survey-is-classified-as-either-anonymous-of-non-anonymous">Types - Each survey is classified as either Anonymous of Non-anonymous<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-each-survey-is-classified-as-either-anonymous-of-non-anonymous" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An anonymous survey</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Is used to get feedback from the users allowing them to give prompt feedback anonymously.
No user identifiable data will be recorded for the responses they will provide including usernames, identification particulars address etc.</p>
<p>A non-anonymous survey</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Allow you as a survey administrator to know who is giving feedback and what feedback he/she is giving.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  In this survey type username (if user is logged in), identification particulars address, country details are recorded.</p>
<p>Sometimes, a survey can be divided into questionnaire and the interview.</p>
<ul>
<li>Questionnaires- are usually paper-and-pencil instruments that the respondent completes.</li>
<li>Interviews - are completed by the interviewer based on the respondent says</li>
</ul>
<p>Process – Good surveys start with clear theory, then the translation of theory into sensible survey questions, pre-testing and revision of questions, development and pre-testing of the survey instrument, sampling, data gathering, and, finally, data analysis.</p>
<p>The following is the process of planning and conducting a survey:</p>
<p>Decide on your goals</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Before you can start your research, you will need to form a clear picture in your mind of the expected outcome.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Identify the overall reasons for conducting the survey.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> What will you know after you have conducted the survey? Do you need feedback on a product or your service? Is the information you are looking for of a general nature or very specific? Do you have a particular audience in mind, or will you be sending out online surveys to the general public?</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The answers to these questions will help you to decide how to target your survey.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Determine the deadline for reporting the data the survey will collect. This will ensure you complete the survey on time</p>
<ul>
<li>Design the methodology for conducting the survey</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Decide the procedures for conducting the survey: the number of people you will survey (sample size), how you will survey them (self-administered questionnaire or interview)</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a list of questions</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Identify the questions you want the data to answer.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> There are many different types of questions that can be used on a survey, like open questions, closed questions, matrix table questions, and single- or multi-response questions.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> One of the benefits of designing an online survey is that participants don't have to fill in questions that are not relevant to them. Based on their answers certain questions can be skipped.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Develop the tools and pretest them</p>
<ul>
<li>Invite the participants</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Who you want to take part in your survey will help you to decide on the best contact method.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Identify the study respondents and enumerators</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> You can send an email or call the participants</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Train them and assign them responsibilities</p>
<ul>
<li>Gather your responses</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Determine when to start the data collection</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is important to assign a unique code to each participant to make sure that they only take part in your survey once.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Distribute survey forms. As they are returned, track the number completed.</p>
<ul>
<li>Analyze the results</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Analyze your date according to your objectives.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Make visual representations of the data by presenting the results in tables and graphs.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> You can also print out the data in the form of a spreadsheet, which can then be used for further analysis.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> There are several software packages available for data analysis (Epi-info, SPSS, SAS, STATA, RA)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Present the analyzed report in Narratives, Graphs, Charts, Tables or Pictures</p>
<ul>
<li>Write a report</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The final step in conducting online surveys is to write a report explaining your findings.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> A successful survey will provide the answers to the questions you had about your business, product or service.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Use proper report writing layout</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ Provide summary of your results</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biased-samples">Biased samples<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biased-samples" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There are errors that may lead to inaccuracy when completing survey tools</li>
<li>Biased sample means a sample has some favors on a particular subject.</li>
<li>The following are causes of biasness:</li>
<li>Unrepresentative sample - Bias often occurs when the survey sample does not accurately represent the population. It is also called selection bias.</li>
<li>Under coverage - occurs when some members of the population are inadequately represented in the sample</li>
<li>Nonresponse bias - Sometimes, individuals chosen for the sample are unwilling or unable to participate in the survey.</li>
<li>Voluntary response bias - Voluntary response bias occurs when sample members are self-selected volunteers, as in voluntary samples</li>
<li>Measurement Error - A poor measurement process can also lead to bias</li>
<li>Response bias - refers to the bias that results from problems in the response process. Some examples of response bias are given below:</li>
<li>Leading questions - The wording of the question may be loaded in some way to unduly favor one response over another.</li>
<li>Social desirability - Most people like to present themselves in a favorable light, so they will be reluctant to admit to unsavory attitudes or illegal activities in a survey, particularly if survey results are not confidential. Instead, their responses may be biased toward what they believe is socially desirable.</li>
<li>Biased sample can be eliminated by applying random sampling procedures.</li>
<li>Random sampling is a procedure for sampling from a population in which:</li>
<li>The selection of a sample unit is based on chance</li>
<li>Every element of the population has a known, non-zero probability of being selected.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="response-rate">Response rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#response-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Response rate - refers to the number of people who answered the survey divided by the number of people in the sample. It is also known as completion rate or return rate. It is usually expressed in the form of a percentage.</li>
<li>The following are ways of increasing response rate:</li>
<li>☑ Offering an incentive to the participant, for example, you can offer a gift, the chance of winning something in a lottery, a donation to charity, or a point’s accumulation system where participant can save up points that can be exchanged for gifts.</li>
<li>☑ Promising to share the results with your participants.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="points-to-be-considered-when-constructing-a-survey-tool">Points to be considered when constructing a survey tool<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-be-considered-when-constructing-a-survey-tool" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Open ended questions with probes</li>
<li>Simple and brief questions</li>
<li>Avoid closed questions</li>
<li>Avoid leading questions</li>
<li>Start with most easy questions</li>
<li>Make personal questions last</li>
<li>Each question to address one issue</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>When writing the questions, keep the language very simple and avoid ambiguity or double negations.</li>
<li>Make questions specific</li>
<li>Ask questions in a logical order</li>
<li>Construct response categories carefully – let it not be too long</li>
<li>Provide clear and sufficient instructions or directions including reasons for the survey</li>
</ul>
