<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="errors-leading-to-inaccuracy-when-constructing-a-survey-tool">Errors leading to inaccuracy when constructing a survey tool<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#errors-leading-to-inaccuracy-when-constructing-a-survey-tool" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Unclear objectives</li>
<li>Questions not matching the survey objectives</li>
<li>Questions are ambiguous</li>
<li>Tool doesn't provide adequate space for data entry</li>
<li>Questions are not well numbered</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="survey-report-presentation">Survey report presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#survey-report-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Every survey must have a report. This can be a brief summary (abstract) of detailed report</li>
<li>Abstract – provides a one paged summary of the survey report in terms of:</li>
<li>Title, authors, particulars and introduction</li>
<li>Methodology</li>
<li>Key findings</li>
<li>Recommendations</li>
<li>A detailed report is voluminous and it contains the following:</li>
<li>Title page (table of content, acknowledgements, list of abbreviations, executive summary/preface or abstract)</li>
<li>Chapter 1 – Background and introduction</li>
<li>Chapter 2 – Literature review</li>
<li>Chapter 3 – Methodology/data collection process</li>
<li>Chapter 4 – Findings/data results and interpretations</li>
<li>Chapter 5 – Discussions of the findings using your own thoughts and opinion</li>
<li>Chapter 6 – Conclusions and recommendations – this can also include detailed implementation plan</li>
<li>Reference</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="evaluation-and-feedback">Evaluation and feedback<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-and-feedback" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Evaluation – is an appraisal of something to determine its worth or fitness.</li>
<li>It can be done before starting a project (Formative) or after completion of the project (Summative)</li>
<li>The reasons for evaluation are:</li>
<li>It can assist an organization, program, project or any other intervention or initiative to assess any aim, realizable concept/proposal, or any alternative,</li>
<li>To help in decision-making;</li>
<li>To ascertain the degree of achievement or value in regard to the aim and objectives and results of any such action that has been completed.¹</li>
<li>Is to enable reflection and assist in the identification of future change</li>
<li>Determines if specific program strategies were implemented as planned</li>
<li>Focuses on program implementation</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Helps to draw conclusions about five main aspects of the intervention:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Relevance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Effectiveness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Efficiency - Finally, cost-benefit or cost-effectiveness analysis assesses the efficiency of a program. Evaluators outline the benefits and cost of the program for comparison. An efficient program has a lower cost-benefit ratio.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impact</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sustainability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Program evaluations can involve both quantitative and qualitative methods of social research</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring is a systematic and routine collection of information from projects and programmes for four main purposes:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To learn from experiences to improve practices and activities in the future;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To have internal and external accountability of the resources used and the results obtained;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To take informed decisions on the on-running actions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring and evaluation uses indicators to for measurement and in drawing conclusions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indicators are statistics used to measure current conditions as well as forecasting or predicting trends. They measure change over time. Indicators can be:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Input – measures efforts put in</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Process – measures procedures</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Output – measures immediate results</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Outcome – measures changes that comes as a result of the outputs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring and evaluation is implemented through a logical framework (commonly known as log-frame)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The monitoring and evaluation log frame include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Objectives of the program</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Activities implemented</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Measurable indicators</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Means of verification</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>M&amp;E Log frame</p>

Distribute Chlorine to every homes</td><td># of homes supplied with chlorine</td><td>Household survey</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td># of homes with patients with diarrhea</td><td>Household survey</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td># of chlorines distributed per home</td><td>Distribution list</td></tr></tbody></table>

<ul>
<li>In any survey, there must be feedback</li>
<li>A survey feedback is a process in which community members complete questionnaires on various issues, receive feedback on the results, and then take appropriate actions to address the critical needs and concerns.</li>
<li>The objectives of survey feedback are:</li>
<li>To assist the organization in diagnosing its problems and developing action plan for problem-solving.</li>
<li>To assist the group members to improve the relationships through discussion of common problems.</li>
<li>The following are the processes of survey feedback:</li>
<li>Data Collection - The first step in survey feedback is data collection usually by a consultant based on a structured questionnaire.</li>
<li>Feedback of Information - After the data are analyzed, feedback is given to the persons who have participated in the fulfilling up of questionnaire. The feedback may be given either orally or in a written form. In oral system of feedback, it is provided through group discussion or problem-solving sessions conducted by the consultant.</li>
<li>Follow-up Action - Survey feedback programme is not meaningful unless some follow-up action is taken based on the data collected. One such follow-up action may be to advise the participants to develop their own action plans to overcome the problems revealed by the consultant.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-strategy">Community strategy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-strategy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Improve understanding on community strategy</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>To understand the meaning and objectives of community strategy</li>
<li>To define the household and community roles in community strategy</li>
<li>To understand the implementation process of community strategy</li>
<li>Improve knowledge on community involvement and participation in sustaining health programs</li>
<li>To gain practical experience on community units</li>
</ul>
<p>Community strategy - this is an approach that sets up an assurance that Kenyan communities have the capacity and motivation to take up their essential role in health care delivery</p>
<p>National Health Sector Strategic Plan – This is a five year plan that aims at reversing the declining trends in key health sector indicators. The NHSSP II has five broad policy objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increase equitable access to health services</li>
<li>Improve the quality and responsiveness of services in the sector</li>
<li>Improve the efficiency and effectiveness of service delivery</li>
<li>Enhance the regulatory capacity of MOH</li>
<li>Foster partnerships in improving health and delivering services</li>
<li>Improve the financing of the health sector</li>
</ul>
<p>Kenya Essential Health Package of Health - KEPH is an approach that supports the achievement of the goals of the second National Health Sector Strategic Plan, 2005–2010 (NHSSP II). The packages are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Eliminate communicable conditions</li>
<li>Revise rising burden of non-communicable conditions</li>
<li>Reduce the burden of violence and injuries</li>
<li>Provide essential health services</li>
<li>Minimize exposure of health risk factors</li>
<li>Strengthen collaboration with other related health sectors</li>
</ul>
<p>Household – It consists of one or more people who live in the same dwelling and also share at meals or living accommodation, and may consist of a single family or some other grouping of people. A single dwelling will be considered to contain multiple households if either meals or living space are not shared.</p>
<p>Community mobilization – is an attempt to bring both human and non-human resources together to undertake developmental activities in order to achieve sustainable development.</p>
<p>Community involvement – is the process of engaging in dialogue and collaboration with community members</p>
<p>Goal – is a desired result that a person or a system envisions, plans and commits to achieve. The overall goal of the community strategy is to enhance community access to health care in order to improve productivity and thus reduce poverty, hunger, and child and maternal deaths, as well as improve education performance across all the stages of the life cycle.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Objectives – the objectives of community strategy are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>To improve the health status of Kenyan communities through initiation and implementation of life-cycle focused health actions.</li>
<li>Provide level 1 services for all cohorts and socio-economic groups taking in to account their priority needs</li>
<li>Build the capacity of community health extension workers (CHEWs) and community own resource persons (CORPS) to provide services at level 1</li>
<li>Strengthen health facility- community linkages through effective decentralization and partnership</li>
<li>Strengthen the community to progressively realize their rights for accessible and quality care and to seek accountability from facility based health services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-it-came-about">How it came about<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-came-about" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Communities are at the foundation of affordable, equitable and effective health care, and are the core of Kenya Essential Package for Health (KEPH)</li>
<li>The concept came about after seeing the need to enhance community access to health care in order to improve productivity and reduce poverty, hunger and child &amp; maternal dearth as well as improve education performance across all stages of the life cycle</li>
<li>Kenya realized the need of establishing sustainable and decentralized community level services and accountability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="roles-of-households-and-community">Roles of households and community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#roles-of-households-and-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Health promotion – through:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure healthy diet for people at all stages in life in order to meet nutritional need</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Building healthy social capital to ensure mutual support in meeting daily needs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Demand health and social entitlements as citizens</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor health status to promote early detection of problem for timely action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking regular exercise</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure gender equity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use available services to monitor nutrition, chronic conditions and other causes of disability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disease prevention – through:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Practice good personal hygiene in terms of hand washing, use of latrine etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Using safe drinking water</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure adequate shelter and protection against vectors of diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preventing accidents and abuse and taking appropriate measures when they occur</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensuring appropriate sexual behavior to prevent STI</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Care seeking compliance with treatment and advice –through:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Giving sick household members appropriate home care for illness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking children for immunization as scheduled</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Recognizing and acting on the need for referral or seeking care outside home</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Following recommendations given by health worker in relation to treatment, follow up and referral</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensuring that every pregnant woman receives antenatal and maternity care services</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Governance and management of health services – through:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attending and taking an active part in meetings to discuss:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Trends in coverage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Morbidity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Resources and clients satisfaction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Claiming rights – through:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Knowing what rights communities have in health</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Building capacity to claim these rights progressively</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensuring that health workers in the community are accountable for effective health service delivery and resource use</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure health facilities are functioning in line with the Citizen Health Charter</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implementation-framework-and-process">Implementation framework and process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implementation-framework-and-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Organizational structure of coordination</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Structure</th><th>Summary of activities</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Household, village, school, congregation</td><td>• Plan, implement, monitor, evaluate and provide feedback on activities</td></tr><tr><td>• Mobilize and manage resources</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Undertake health promotion, hygiene, lifestyle and care seeking initiatives</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Sub location, parish, dispensary</td><td>• Provide health status information</td></tr><tr><td>• Support, provide and protect water</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Manage CBHIS</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Train CORPS Establish and maintain linkages</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Division, health centre</td><td>• Provide training and support supervision</td></tr><tr><td>• Coordinate, collaborate, network, pool resources</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>District, diocese, hospital</td><td>• Comprehensive district planning</td></tr><tr><td>• Strengthen health boards</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Facilitate M&amp;E and coordinate NGOs</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Train leaders and extension staff</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Province</td><td>• Technical support</td></tr><tr><td>• Build capacity of districts</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>National</td><td>• Formulate guidelines and policy</td></tr><tr><td>• Build capacity of districts and province</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Multi-sector and donor coordination</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Ensure CBHIS is part of the HMIS</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>• Quality assurance</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li>The entry steps</li>
<li>Define a clear implementation guideline</li>
<li>Create awareness among district leaders</li>
<li>Form and equip district-level multi-sector working groups and training teams</li>
<li>Follow up, monitor and evaluate</li>
<li>Launch the program in the communities. This will follow steps like:</li>
<li>Exploration</li>
<li>Protocol</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Participatory assessment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The assessment should include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The population</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community structures</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any existing community information systems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Resource availability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication strategy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Service delivery and the minimum package of care and support</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health status</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Food security</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The environment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Feedback and participatory planning of level 1 service activities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Findings of the assessment are presented to the community in a general meeting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The community validates the findings</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The community summarizes the findings</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Strategic action points are based on strengths and opportunities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Actions are categorized in to:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those that can be taken by the CORPS</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those that require additional support from local partners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those that require external support</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Community mobilization - This is the process of bringing the community members together. It is an attempt to bring both human and non-human resources together to undertake developmental activities in order to achieve sustainable development</p>
<ul>
<li>is a process through which action is stimulated by a community itself that is planned, carried out, and evaluated by a community's individuals, groups, and organizations on a participatory and sustained basis to improve the health, hygiene and education levels so as to enhance the overall standard of living in the community</li>
<li>is a process which begins a dialogue among members of the community to determine who, what, and how issues are decided,</li>
<li>The process of sensitizing and motivating the community to work together</li>
<li>Effective mobilization will ensure the community's interest is created and community members are motivated and influenced to take action and participate</li>
<li>Mobilization is done through community gatherings, baraza, village health days, women and youth groups</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-of-community-mobilization">Steps of community mobilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-of-community-mobilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Getting to know the community, provide information &amp; create interest</li>
<li>Analysis + Identification resources + Problem identification + Identification solutions &amp; projects</li>
<li>Decision making &amp; selection of leaders by community</li>
<li>Identification of stakeholders</li>
<li>Planning &amp; selection of implementing leader</li>
<li>Project implementation by community</li>
<li>Follow-up &amp; monitoring</li>
<li>Evaluation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tasks-in-community-mobilization">Tasks in community mobilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tasks-in-community-mobilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Developing an on-going dialogue between community members</li>
<li>Creating or strengthening community organizations (Committees etc.)</li>
<li>Creating an environment in which individuals can empower themselves to address their own and their community's needs</li>
<li>Promoting community members' participation</li>
</ul>
<p>Community involvement and participation - Community involvement is the process of letting the community members play active role in any activity. A project is more likely to fail if there is no community 'buy in' - Sometimes this is because the project was introduced by 'experts' who had their own ideas about what should be done. This is called the top-down approach</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Importance of community involvement and participation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It promote ownership and accountability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ CORPS learn much faster when they participate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Community can participate in health promotion, advocacy, follow up</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It is often better to use a participatory approach to ensure the project's sustainability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ The participation helps to ensure that programmes are equitable and effective.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participation can positively impact the health, well-being and safety.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Communities have different needs, problems, beliefs, practices, assets, and resources related to sexual health. Getting the community involved in program design and implementation helps ensure that strategies are appropriate for and acceptable to the community and its youth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Community participation promotes shared responsibility by service providers, community members, and youth themselves for the sexual health of adolescents in the community.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Community participation can increase the accountability of sexual health programs and service providers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participation can empower youth within the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Key messages to community involvement and participation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Special attention should be given to ensuring that all groups are able to participate, including those with specific needs and/or those who are marginalized and lacking a voice in decision-making.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participation structures and procedures may require targeted effort and additional resources; it is an essential way of reinforcing a sense of dignity, reducing vulnerability and helping to build local capacity without undermining peoples' own coping strategies in times of crisis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participation should be based on assessments of existing structures which can be used to support participatory methods.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participatory approaches should respect local culture there needs to be due regard for culturally-embedded power relationships which may be exploitative or oppressive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Participation and community involvement should be planned and integrated into all stages of the project cycle – assessment, planning, implementation, monitoring and evaluation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ A community's members are a rich source of knowledge about their community and of energy and commitment to that community</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedures-of-community-based-research">Procedures of community based research<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedures-of-community-based-research" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Purposes of community based research:</li>
<li>☐ There is increased focus of funding agencies and researchers on approaches to public health research</li>
<li>☐ Influence of social and political systems on behavioral and health outcomes</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Principles of community-based research:</li>
<li>☑ Respect for community interests that go beyond those of individual potential research subjects</li>
<li>☑ Identification of potential community stakeholders as well as individual research subjects.</li>
<li>☑ Inform the community stakeholders and potential research subjects about the research.</li>
<li>☑ Invite feedback regarding concerns about the research from community stakeholders and individual potential research subjects.</li>
<li>☑ Partnership establishment</li>
<li>☑ Respect the community partner's interest in the project and be open to ways that the community might benefit or want to use the information.</li>
<li>☑ Disseminate research findings to both community stakeholders and individual research subjects.</li>
<li>☑ Having the research topic address a community-defined need, question or problem, and strive to combine knowledge with action to achieve necessary changes.</li>
<li>☑ Recognizing the research as a partnership and be open to the guidance of community insight and experience.</li>
<li>☑ Having the partnership appropriately balance power and decision-making between the researchers and the community participants in a way that is mutually acceptable.</li>
<li>☑ Partners making clear and open communication an ongoing priority by striving to understand each other's needs and self-interests.</li>
<li>☑ Partners recognizing race, ethnicity, class, and other aspects of culture matter and talk openly about these issues.</li>
<li>☑ Feedback among all stakeholders in the partnership, with the goals of continuously improving the partnership and its outcomes.</li>
<li>☑ Realizing partnerships can dissolve and plan a process for closure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="income-generating-activities">Income generating activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#income-generating-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a mechanism for sustainability</li>
<li>The CORPS get involved in activities that give them revolving funds</li>
<li>Some of the IGAs include kitchen gardening, poultry raring, merry-go-round (chama)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skills-in-training-a-community-resource-person">Skills in training a community resource person<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skills-in-training-a-community-resource-person" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Adult learn best through illustrated lectures, discussions, brainstorming, group work and feedback, role plays, demonstration, community or household visit, transect walk in PRA, observation and resource mapping.</li>
<li>Adult learning theory: problem-based and collaborative</li>
<li>Principles of adult learning:</li>
<li>Adults are internally motivated and self-directed</li>
<li>Adult learners resist learning when they feel others are imposing information, ideas or actions on them.</li>
<li>A facilitator should:</li>
<li>Set up a graded learning program and do not overloading for the student.</li>
<li>Develop rapport with the student and show interest in their opinion</li>
<li>Lead the student toward inquiry before supplying them with too many facts.</li>
<li>Provide regular constructive and specific feedback</li>
<li>Review goals and acknowledge goal completion</li>
<li>Encourage use of learning resources</li>
<li>Acknowledge the preferred learning style of the student.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Adults bring life experiences and knowledge to learning experiences</p>
<p>✓ Adults like to be given opportunity to use their existing knowledge and experience gained from life experience, and applies it to their new learning experiences.
✓ Find out about your student - their interests and past experiences
✓ Assist them to draw on those experiences
✓ Facilitate reflective learning opportunities</p>
<p>○ Adults are goal oriented</p>
<p>✓ Adult students become ready to learn when "they experience a need to learn it in order to cope more satisfyingly with real-life tasks or problems"
As educator, you can:
○ Provide meaningful learning experiences
○ Provide real case-studies
○ Ask questions that motivate reflection, inquiry and further research.</p>
<p>○ Adults are relevancy oriented</p>
<p>✓ Adult learners want to know the relevance of what they are learning to what they want to achieve.
✓ Ways of helping learners see the value of their observations and practical experiences are:
○ Ask the student to do some reflection
○ Provide some choice of fieldwork project by providing two or more options, so that learning is more likely to reflect the student's interests.</p>
<p>○ Adults are practical</p>
<p>✓ Students move from classroom mode to hands-on problem solving
A trainer should:
○ Clearly explain your clinical reasoning.
○ Be explicit.
○ Promote active participation</p>
<p>○ Adult learners like to be respected</p>
<p>✓ Respect can be demonstrated to your student by:
○ Taking interest
○ Acknowledging the wealth of experiences that the student brings to the placement;
○ Regarding them as a colleague who is equal in life experience
○ Encouraging expression of ideas, reasoning and feedback at every opportunity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="environment-and-health">Environment and Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment-and-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Understand the role of environment in our health</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe environmental factors that affect our health</li>
<li>Describe the relationship of man with the environment</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Environment – is anything that externally surrounds a man. This is where man lives. The World Health Organization (WHO) defines environment, as it relates to health, as “all the physical, chemical, and biological factors external to a person, and all the related behaviors.”</p>
<p>Environmental health – is the relationship between environment and health</p>
<p>Belief – is an acceptance that a statement is true or that something exists. It can also be defined as an acceptance that something exists or is true, especially one without proof</p>
<p>Culture - Culture refers to the cumulative deposit of knowledge, experience, beliefs, values, attitudes, meanings, hierarchies, religion, notions of time, roles, spatial relations, concepts of the universe, and material objects and possessions acquired by a group of people in the course of generations through individual and group striving</p>
<p>Environmental components – these are what makes up the environment. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>PHYSICAL: - e.g. air, water, soil, housing, climate, geography, heat, light, noise, debris, radiation</li>
<li>BIOLOGICAL – e.g. Man, viruses, microbial agents, insects, rodents, animals and plants, etc.</li>
<li>PSYCHOSOCIAL – e.g. Cultural values, customs, beliefs, habits, attitudes, morals, religion, education, lifestyles, community life, health services, social and political organization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-environmental-health">Importance of environmental health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-environmental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Goal of environmental health is to promote health for all through a healthy environment.</li>
<li>Environmental health consists of preventing or controlling disease, injury, and disability related to the interactions between people and their environment.</li>
<li>It increasing quality of life and years of healthy life</li>
<li>Globally, nearly 25 percent of all deaths and the total disease burden can be attributed to environmental factors such as:</li>
<li>Exposure to hazardous substances in the air, water, soil, and food</li>
<li>Natural and technological disasters</li>
<li>Emergencies</li>
<li>Water supply</li>
<li>Increased urban development</li>
<li>Physical hazards</li>
<li>Nutritional deficiencies</li>
<li>Poor environmental quality has its greatest impact on people whose health status is already at risk.</li>
<li>Therefore, environmental health must address the societal and environmental factors that increase the likelihood of exposure and disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environmental-health-factors-risks-affecting-our-health">Environmental health factors (risks) affecting our health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-health-factors-risks-affecting-our-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Environmental health risks are factors outside of the body that can affect a person's wellbeing.
Examples include:</li>
<li>Air pollution – for example, smog, wood smoke and mould</li>
<li>Water quality – for example, grey water, tank water, fluoridation and drought.</li>
<li>Food quality and safety – for example, contamination and nutrition.</li>
<li>Chemicals – for example, pesticides, farm chemicals.</li>
<li>Metals – for example, exposure to lead, mercury</li>
<li>Diseases from animals and insects (vector borne) – for example, dengue fever, virus, malaria.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Infectious diseases – for example, viral infections like swine flu.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Natural hazards – for example, solar radiation and extreme weather events.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Man-made structures – for example, exposure to asbestos or electromagnetic radiation sources like mobile phones.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occupational health – for example, safety issues relating to the workplace such as noise pollution and hazardous waste.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Climate change – for example, higher sea levels, increased soil salinity and increased temperatures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Housing conditions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preventing or reducing the risk of illness, injury or disease in the community is important for environmental health.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="understanding-environmental-health">Understanding Environmental Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#understanding-environmental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The following are 6 themes that draw attention to elements of the environment and their linkages to health.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="outdoor-air-quality">Outdoor Air Quality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#outdoor-air-quality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poor air quality is linked to premature death, cancer, and long-term damage to respiratory and cardiovascular systems.</li>
<li>Decreasing air pollution is an important step in creating a healthy environment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surface-and-ground-water">Surface and Ground Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surface-and-ground-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Surface and ground water quality applies to both drinking water and recreational waters.</li>
<li>Contamination by infectious agents or chemicals can cause mild to severe illness.</li>
<li>Protecting water sources and minimizing exposure to contaminated water sources are important parts of environmental health.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="toxic-substances-and-hazardous-wastes">Toxic Substances and Hazardous Wastes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toxic-substances-and-hazardous-wastes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The health effects of toxic substances and hazardous wastes are not yet fully understood. Research to better understand how these exposures may impact health is ongoing.</li>
<li>Meanwhile, efforts to reduce exposures continue.</li>
<li>Reducing exposure to toxic substances and hazardous wastes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="homes-and-communities">Homes and Communities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#homes-and-communities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>People spend most of their time at home, work, or school. Some of these environments may expose people to:</li>
<li>Indoor air pollution</li>
<li>Inadequate heating and sanitation</li>
<li>Structural problems</li>
<li>Electrical and fire hazards</li>
<li>Lead-based paint hazards</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infrastructure-and-surveillance">Infrastructure and Surveillance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infrastructure-and-surveillance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevention of exposure to environmental hazards relies on many partners, including state and local health departments.</li>
<li>Personnel, surveillance systems, and education are important resources for investigating and responding to disease, monitoring for hazards, and educating the public.</li>
<li>Additional methods and greater capacity to measure and respond to environmental hazards are needed.</li>
</ul>

<li>Diseases can be reduced by improving water quality and sanitation and increasing access to adequate water and sanitation facilities.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="responsibilities-if-health-teams-in-environmental-health">Responsibilities if health teams in environmental health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#responsibilities-if-health-teams-in-environmental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physician">Physician<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physician" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Screening patients at risk for hereditable conditions and potentially preventable disorders</li>
<li>Assessment, diagnosis, primary medical treatment and advice for management of acute medical conditions and injuries</li>
<li>Assessment of the exacerbations and complications of chronic medical problems</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nurses">Nurses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Complete health assessments, including a health history and physical examination</li>
<li>Formulate and communicate medical diagnoses</li>
<li>Synthesize information from patients to identify broader implications for health within the family</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-culture-influences-health-key-points">How Culture Influences Health -Key points<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-culture-influences-health-key-points" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Culture is a pattern of ideas, customs and behaviors shared by a particular people or society. It is constantly evolving.</li>
<li>The speed of cultural evolution varies. It increases when a group migrates to and incorporates components of a new culture into their culture of origin.</li>
<li>Children often struggle with being ‘between cultures’– balancing the ‘old’ and the ‘new’. They essentially belong to both, whereas their parents often belong predominantly to the ‘old’ culture.</li>
<li>The influence of culture on health is vast:</li>
<li>It affects perceptions of health, illness and death,</li>
<li>Beliefs about causes of disease</li>
<li>Approaches to health promotion</li>
<li>How illness and pain are experienced and expressed, where patients seek help</li>
<li>The types of treatment patients prefer.</li>
<li>Both health professionals and patients are influenced by their respective cultures.</li>
<li>Cultural bias may result in very different health-related preferences and perceptions.</li>
<li>Demonstrating awareness of a patient’s culture can promote trust, better health care, lead to higher rates of acceptance of diagnoses and improve treatment adherence.</li>
<li>Acceptance of a diagnosis, including who should be told, when and how.</li>
<li>Acceptance of preventive or health promotion measures (e.g., vaccines, prenatal care, birth control, screening tests, etc.).</li>
<li>Perceptions of death, dying and who should be involved</li>
<li>Willingness to discuss symptoms with a health care provider, or with an interpreter being present.</li>
<li>Influence of family dynamics, including traditional gender roles, filial responsibilities, and patterns of support among family members.</li>
<li>How accessible the health system is, as well as how well it functions.</li>
</ul>

<li>Technology</li>
<li>Agricultural land los and soil erosion</li>
<li>Energy industry pollution</li>
<li>Creation of infrastructure</li>
<li>Coal mining and burning</li>
<li>Pharmaceuticals and personal care products</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-community-in-preserving-healthy-and-safe-environments">Role of community in preserving Healthy and Safe Environments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-community-in-preserving-healthy-and-safe-environments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-can-state-local-and-territorial-governments-do">What can state, local and territorial governments do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-state-local-and-territorial-governments-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Facilitate collaboration among diverse sectors (e.g., planning, housing, transportation, energy, education, environmental regulation, agriculture, business associations, labor organizations, health and public health) when making decisions likely to have a significant effect on health.</li>
<li>Include health criteria as a component of decision making (e.g., policy making, land use and transportation planning).</li>
<li>Conduct comprehensive community health needs assessments and develop state and community health improvement plans.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Strengthen and enforce housing and sanitary code requirements and ensure rapid remediation or alternative housing options.</li>
<li>Participate in national voluntary accreditation of health departments.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-businesses-and-employers-do">What Can Businesses and Employers Do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-businesses-and-employers-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ensure that homes and workplaces are healthy, including eliminating safety hazards (e.g., trip hazards, unsafe stairs), ensuring that buildings are free of water intrusion, indoor environmental pollutants (e.g., radon, mold, tobacco smoke), and pests, and performing regular maintenance of heating and cooling systems.</li>
<li>Adopt practices to increase physical activity and reduce pollution.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-health-care-systems-insurers-and-clinicians-do">What Can Health Care Systems, Insurers, and Clinicians Do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-health-care-systems-insurers-and-clinicians-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Partner with state, local, and territorial governments, business leaders, and community-based organizations to conduct comprehensive community health needs assessments and develop community health improvement plans.</li>
<li>Support integration of prevention and public health skills into health care professional training and cross train health care practitioners to implement prevention strategies.</li>
<li>Increase the use of certified equipment and skilled personnel</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-early-learning-centers-schools-colleges-and-universities-do">What Can Early Learning Centers, Schools, Colleges, and Universities Do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-early-learning-centers-schools-colleges-and-universities-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Implement policies and practices that promote healthy and safe environments (e.g., improving indoor air quality; addressing mold problems; reducing exposure to pesticides and lead; ensuring that drinking water sources are free from bacteria and other toxins; implementing and enforcing tobacco free policies).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-community-non-profit-and-faith-based-organizations-do">What Can Community, Non-Profit, and Faith-Based Organizations Do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-community-non-profit-and-faith-based-organizations-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Convene diverse partners and promote strong cross-sector participation in planning, implementing, and evaluating community health efforts.</li>
<li>Implement processes to ensure that people are actively engaged in decisions that affect health.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-can-individuals-and-families-do">What Can Individuals and Families Do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-can-individuals-and-families-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use alternative transportation (e.g., biking, walking, public transportation, car and vanpooling).</li>
<li>Conduct home assessments and modifications (e.g., installing smoke and carbon monoxide detectors, testing for lead, checking for mold and radon).</li>
<li>Purchase energy-efficient products, support local vendors, and recycle.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-barriers-to-inter-professional-healthcare-team-work">Common barriers to inter-professional healthcare team work<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-barriers-to-inter-professional-healthcare-team-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="organizational-barriers">Organizational barriers:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizational-barriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Lack of knowledge and appreciation of the roles of other health professionals;</li>
<li>Compelling arguments for team building to senior decision-makers;</li>
<li>Lack of outcomes research on collaboration;</li>
<li>Financial and regulatory constraints;</li>
<li>Legal issues of scope of practice and liability;</li>
<li>Reimbursement structures for different professions, including which services receive</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Hierarchical administrative and educational structures that discourage inter-professional collaboration.</li>
</ul>
<p>Barriers at the team level:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lack of a clearly stated, shared, and measurable purpose;</li>
<li>Lack of training in inter-professional collaboration;</li>
<li>Role and leadership ambiguity;</li>
<li>Team too large or too small;</li>
<li>Team not composed of appropriate professionals;</li>
<li>Lack of appropriate mechanism for timely exchange of information;</li>
<li>Need for orientation for new members;</li>
<li>Lack of framework for problem discovery and resolution;</li>
<li>Difference in levels of authority, power, expertise, income;</li>
<li>Difficulty in engaging the community;</li>
<li>Traditions/professional cultures, particularly medicine's history of hierarchy;</li>
<li>Lack of commitment of team members;</li>
<li>Different goals of individual team members;</li>
<li>Apathy of team members;</li>
<li>Inadequate decision making; and</li>
<li>Conflict regarding individual relationships to the patient/client.</li>
</ul>
<p>Barriers faced by individual team members:</p>
<ul>
<li>Split loyalties between team and own discipline;</li>
<li>Multiple responsibilities and job titles;</li>
<li>Competition</li>
<li>Gender, race, or class-based prejudice;</li>
<li>Persistence of a defensive attitude;</li>
<li>Reluctance to accept suggestions from team members representing other professions; and</li>
<li>Lack of trust in the collaborative process.</li>
<li>Barriers for independent providers:</li>
<li>Accustomed to assuming total responsibility;</li>
<li>Unease with allowing others to be involved in clinical decision-making;</li>
<li>Discomfort with performance review by team members of different professional backgrounds;</li>
<li>Legal liability for others' decisions; and</li>
<li>Dilution of traditional one-to-one relationship with patient/client.</li>
</ul>
<p>Overcoming barriers</p>
<ul>
<li>Agree on unifying philosophy centered around primary care of the patient/client and the community;</li>
<li>Develop a commitment to the common goal of collaboration;</li>
<li>Learn about other professions;</li>
<li>Respect others' skills and knowledge;</li>
<li>Establish positive attitudes about own profession;</li>
<li>Develop trust between members;</li>
<li>Be willing to share responsibility for patient/client care;</li>
<li>Establish a mechanism for negotiation and re-negotiation of goals and roles over time;</li>
<li>Establish method for resolving conflicts between team members; and</li>
<li>Be willing to work continuously on overcoming barriers.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Drugs and substance abuse</p>
<p>Goal: Understand common drugs abused and ways of controlling drug abuse</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Discuss commonly abused drugs and its effects in our health</li>
<li>Gain skills and knowledge on behavior change communication</li>
</ul>
<p>Drug abuse – is the excessive use of a substance, especially alcohol or a drug. This is a compulsive, excessive, and self-damaging use of habit forming drugs or substances, leading to addiction or dependence, serious physiological injury (such as damage to kidneys, liver, heart) and/or psychological harm (such as dysfunctional behavior patterns, hallucinations, memory loss), or death. Also called substance abuse</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classifications-of-drugs">Classifications of drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classifications-of-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drugs may be categorized or classified according to certain shared symptomatology or effects. Drugs from each of these categories can affect a person's central nervous system and impair a person's normal faculties, including a person's ability to safely operate a motor vehicle.</p>
<ul>
<li>Central Nervous System (CNS) Depressants - CNS Depressants slow down the operations of the brain and the body. Examples include alcohol, barbiturates, anti-anxiety tranquilizers (e.g., Valium, Librium, Xanax, Prozac, and Thorazine)</li>
<li>CNS Stimulants - CNS Stimulants accelerate the heart rate and elevate the blood pressure and "speed-up" or over-stimulate the body. Examples include Cocaine, "Crack", Amphetamines and Methamphetamine ("Crank").</li>
<li>Hallucinogens - Hallucinogens cause the user to perceive things differently than they actually are. Examples include LSD, Peyote, Psilocybin and MDMA (Ecstasy).</li>
<li>Dissociative Anesthetics - It includes drugs that inhibit pain by cutting off or dissociating the brain's perception of the pain. PCP and its analogs are examples of Dissociative Anesthetics.</li>
<li>Narcotic Analgesics - A narcotic analgesic relieves pain, induces euphoria and creates mood changes in the user. Examples of narcotic analgesics include Opium, Codeine, Heroin, Demerol, Darvon, Morphine, Methadone, Vicodin and OxyContin.</li>
<li>Inhalants - Inhalants include a wide variety of breathable substances that produce mind-altering results and effects. Examples include Toluene, plastic cement, paint, gasoline, paint thinners, hair sprays and various anesthetic gases.</li>
<li>Cannabis - Cannabis is the scientific name for marijuana. The active ingredient in cannabis is delta-9 tetrahydrocannabinol. This category includes cannabinoids and synthetics like Dronabinol.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commonly-abused-drugs">Commonly abused drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commonly-abused-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Alcohol - In chemistry, an alcohol is any organic compound in which the hydroxyl functional group is bound to a saturated carbon atom. The term alcohol originally referred to the primary alcohol ethyl alcohol, the predominant alcohol in alcoholic beverages</li>
<li>Tobacco - is a product prepared from the leaves of the tobacco plant by curing them. The plant is categorized within the genus Nicotiana of the Solanaceae (nightshade) family</li>
<li>Marijuana - Cannabis, also known as marijuana and by numerous other names, is a preparation of the Cannabis plant intended for use as a psychoactive drug or medicine</li>
<li>Pain killers - An analgesic or painkiller is any member of the group of drugs used to achieve analgesia, relief from pain. Analgesic drugs act in various ways on the peripheral and central nervous systems</li>
<li>RX sedatives - Prescription medications that act as central nervous system depressants. Barbiturates are prescription sedatives or "sleeping pills" Valium and benzodiazepines are prescription "tranquilizers.</li>
<li>RX stimulants - Prescription stimulants were used historically to treat asthma, obesity, neurological disorders, and a variety of other ailments, before their potential for abuse and addiction became apparent</li>
<li>Cocaine - Cocaine, also known as benzoylmethylecgonine, is a strong stimulant mostly used as a recreational drug. It is commonly snorted, inhaled, or injected into the veins</li>
<li>Hallucinogens - A hallucinogen is a psychoactive agent which can cause hallucinations, perception anomalies, and other substantial subjective changes in thoughts, emotion, and consciousness. The common types of hallucinogens are psychedelics, dissociative, or delirants</li>
<li>Heroin - also known as diamorphine and commonly known by its street names of smack, boy, horse, brown, black, tar, and others is an analgesic originally synthesized by in 1874</li>
</ul>
<p><em><strong>Group work and presentation</strong></em></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="identify-effects-of-drugs-and-substance-abuse-to-individuals-household-and-community">Identify effects of drugs and substance abuse to: Individuals; Household and Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identify-effects-of-drugs-and-substance-abuse-to-individuals-household-and-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Illnesses associated with drug abuse</p>
<ul>
<li>HIV - The human immunodeficiency virus (HIV) causes HIV infection and the acquired immunodeficiency syndrome (AIDS).</li>
<li>Depression - A depressive disorder is a syndrome (group of symptoms) that reflects a sad, blue mood exceeding normal sadness or grief. Depressive disorders are characterized not only by negative thoughts, moods, and behaviors but also by specific changes in bodily functions (for example, eating, sleeping, and sexual activity).</li>
<li>Erectile dysfunction - Erectile dysfunction (ED), also known as impotence, is the inability to achieve or sustain an erection for satisfactory sexual activity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Schizophrenia - Sometimes colloquially but inaccurately referred to as split personality disorder, schizophrenia is a chronic, severe, debilitating mental illness</li>
<li>Steroid withdrawal symptoms - can mimic many other medical problems. Weakness, fatigue, decreased appetite, weight loss, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea (which can lead to fluid and electrolyte abnormalities), and abdominal pain are common. Blood pressure can become too low, leading to dizziness or fainting. Blood sugar levels may drop. Women also may note menstrual changes. Less often, joint pain, muscle aches, fever, mental changes, or elevations of calcium may be noted.</li>
<li>Stress - is a fact of nature in which forces from the inside or outside world affect the individual. The individual responds to stress in ways that affect the individual, as well as their environment. Due to the overabundance of stress in our modern lives, we usually think of stress as a negative experience, but from a biological point of view, stress can be a neutral, negative, or positive experience.</li>
<li>Stroke - also known as a cerebrovascular accident or CVA, occurs when part of the brain loses its blood supply and the part of the body that the blood-deprived brain cells control stops working. This loss of blood supply can be ischemic because of lack of blood flow, or hemorrhagic because of bleeding into brain tissue. A stroke is a medical emergency because strokes can lead to death or permanent disability, plus there are now opportunities to treat ischemic strokes but that treatment needs to be started in the first few hours after the signs of a stroke begin</li>
<li>Hepatitis C infection - is an infection of the liver caused by the hepatitis C virus (HCV). It is difficult for the human immune system to eliminate hepatitis C from the body, and infection with help C usually becomes chronic</li>
<li>Microcephaly - is a medical condition in which the circumference of the head is smaller than normal because the brain has not developed properly or has stopped growing.</li>
<li>Low blood pressure - also called hypotension, is blood pressure low enough that the flow of blood to the organs of the body is inadequate and symptoms and/or signs of low blood flow develop shock.</li>
<li>An aortic aneurysm - involves the aorta, the major artery that leaves the heart to supply blood to the body. An aortic aneurysm is dilation or bulging of the aorta.</li>
<li>Others – child abuse, nose bleeding, brain damage, alcoholism, cancer, Hepatitis B, chronic pain, suicide, antisocial personality disorder, learning disability, sexual problems, anxiety, hypersomnia, hyper sensitivity, domestic violence,</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="behavior-change-communication">Behavior change communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#behavior-change-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Behavior change communication (BCC) is an interactive process of any intervention with individuals, communities to develop communication strategies to promote positive behaviors which are appropriate to their settings.</p>
