<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-health-care">Primary Health Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-health-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Goal: To improve the knowledge and skills on primary health care</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="specific-objectives">Specific objectives:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>To understand the meaning, purpose, origin and levels of primary health care</li>
<li>To explain the pillars and elements of primary health care</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>To understand the implementation of primary health care</li>
<li>To review the successes and failures of primary health care implementation</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Meaning</strong> – Primary Health Care is defined as an essential health care based on practical, scientifically sound, socially acceptable methods, technology made universally acceptable to individuals, families and community through their full participation and affordable cost that the community can sustain and become self-reliant</p>
<p><strong>Purposes</strong> – the importance of primary health care are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reach everybody – particularly those in great need</li>
<li>Reach the home and family levels, and not to be limited to health facilities</li>
<li>Involve a continuity relationship with persons and families</li>
<li>Improving family health – with particular focus on mothers and children</li>
<li>Increase coverage and accessibility of essential health services</li>
<li>Improve the quality of services</li>
<li>Pursue an integrated inter-sectorial and multi-disciplinary approaches</li>
<li>Increase community participation in the planning, delivery, and monitoring of health services</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Origin</strong> – The concept of PHC started as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Declaration of Alma-Ata was adopted in September 1978 at the International Conference on PHC at Almaty (formerly Alma-Ata) in Kazakhstan (formerly Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic)</li>
<li>This was the first international declaration underlining the importance of primary health care</li>
<li>Goals and targets were set for achieving “Health for All” by the Year 2000. Some of these goals were that:</li>
<li>At least 5% of gross national product should be spent on health;</li>
<li>At least 90% of children should have a weight for age that corresponds to the reference values;</li>
<li>Safe water should be available in the home or within 15 minutes’ walking distance, and adequate sanitary facilities should be available in the home or immediate vicinity;</li>
<li>People should have access to trained personnel for attending pregnancy and childbirth; and</li>
<li>Child care should be available up to at least one year of age.</li>
<li>It expressed the need for urgent action by all governments, all health and development workers, and the world community to protect and promote the health of all people</li>
<li>The PHC approach has since then been accepted by member countries of the WHO as the key to achieving the goal of "Health for All".</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Principles</strong> – A principle is a rule that has major influence on the way in which something is done. Therefore, the principles of PHC are rules or guidelines that govern the implementation of PHC’s activities. The five basic principles are:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Equitable distribution</strong></li>
<li>Equity is the fair distribution of available resources to all individuals and families so that they can meet their fundamental and basic needs.</li>
<li>Services should be physically, socially, and financially accessible to everyone</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ People with similar needs should have equal access to similar health services
✓ Equal access, resource distribution and coverage of PHC services should be greatest in those areas with the greatest need</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Manpower development
✓ PHC aims at mobilizing the human potential of the entire community by making use of available resources
✓ This principle facilitates the identification and development of necessary personnel as well as training new categories of health workers to serve the community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community participation
✓ This is the process by which individuals, families and communities take responsibility in promoting their own health and welfare
✓ Full participation is important in decision making and taking care of own health
✓ Community members and health providers need to work together in partnership to seek solutions to problems facing the communities
✓ Communities should participate in: Creating and preserving healthy environment; Maintaining preventive and promotive health; Sharing information about own needs with higher authorities; Implementing health care priorities and managing health facilities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Appropriate technology
✓ This is a kind of technology that is scientifically or technically sound and adoptable to local needs, and the community can afford to maintain it for their self-reliance
✓ Caregivers should be trained to deliver services using the most appropriate and cost-effective methods and equipment for their level of care
✓ Full participation is important in decision making and taking care of own health</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Multi-sector of Inter-sector approach
✓ Health sector cannot achieve much in isolation
✓ PHC requires coordinated effort with other related sectors whose activities impacts on health e.g., agriculture, water and sanitation, transportation &amp; communication, education etc.
✓ The commitment of all sectors may increase if the purpose for joint actions and roles of each sector is clearly defined</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Levels – A level is a stage or position of something. Levels of PHC are the units of care or implementation of activities. The levels of health care are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Individual Based Health Care</li>
<li>Family Based Health Care</li>
<li>Community Based health care</li>
<li>Facility Based Health Care (Dispensary, Health center, District hospital, Provincial hospital)</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Pillars – A pillar a column or support. Pillars of PHC are those support systems that make it achieve goal of improved health by creating partnership between consumers of health services with health care providers. The Seven pillars are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health systems</li>
<li>Priority</li>
<li>Science</li>
<li>Culture</li>
<li>Equity</li>
<li>Participation</li>
<li>Sustainability</li>
</ul>
<p>Elements – Are fundamentals or essentials of PHC. In In the Alma Ata conference of 1978, eight essential elements of PHC were identified. However, individual countries were given the liberty to add any other elements they felt were relevant to their own country. The PHC elements listed at the Alma-Ata declaration were as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Health education</li>
<li>Local disease control</li>
<li>Expanded programme of immunization</li>
<li>Maternal and child health care and family planning</li>
<li>Essential drug supply</li>
<li>Nutrition and adequate food supply</li>
<li>Treatment and prevention of common diseases and injuries</li>
<li>Safe water supply and good sanitation</li>
</ol>
<p>Kenya government has added more elements. These are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Mental Health</li>
<li>Dental Health</li>
<li>Community Based Rehabilitation</li>
<li>HIV/AIDS Prevention</li>
<li>Health information systems</li>
</ol>
<p>Strategies – Are approaches or methods of implementing an activity. There are three main PHC strategies:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Community Based Health Care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ These are health care activities initiated and implemented by community own resource persons</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It is for people of all ages who need health care assistance at home. Community care services include home support, home nursing, physiotherapy and other rehabilitation services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For example: A CHW visits an elderly person at home to help with medication, or a CHW support worker helps a child in a wheel chair with personal care, such as bathing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>BAMAKO Initiative</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ This initiative was a formal statement adopted by African health ministers in 1987 at Bamako in Mali.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ It was meant to implement strategies designed to increase the availability of essential drugs and other health care services for Sub-Saharan Africans</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ This was an initiative of drug revolving funds as income generating activity to sustain PHC</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>activities.</p>
<ul>
<li>Community strategy</li>
<li>☑ This is the concept of taking health services close to the people in the village</li>
<li>☑ It is aimed at taking the Kenya Essential Package for Health to the community. It is a strategy for the delivery of level one service</li>
<li>☑ The overall aim is to involve the communities in addressing the downward trend of deteriorating health status. It is a mechanism through which households and communities take an active role in health and health-related development issues.</li>
</ul>
<p>Roles – Roles are responsibilities assigned to an individual or a group with an aim of achieving a desired objective. The following are key roles of Health Records &amp; Information Officers and Community Health Workers in PHC implementation:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Health Records and Information Officer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Designing, developing and distribution of PHC data collection tools</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Data collection, analysis and dissemination</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Training of CHW on data collection and management</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Advising the PHC team on targets and achievements of PHC</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Monitoring and evaluation of PHC implementation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community Health Workers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Identify and refer patients</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Treatment of minor illnesses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Cary out health education</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Defaulter tracing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Support home based care services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Home follow up</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Success &amp; failures – Are attainment of achievements or inability to attain any intended achievement in any endeavor. The following are reasons why PHC did not achieve its intentions in most of the cross-cutting countries:</p>
<ul>
<li>Many ordinary people felt PHC was a cheap form of healthcare and, if they were able to, they bypassed this level to attend secondary and tertiary centers because of a lack of staff and essential medicines at the PHC level.</li>
<li>Civil war, natural disasters and, more recently, HIV affected the ability of PHC to maintain comprehensive services, especially in many sub-Saharan countries.</li>
<li>Political commitment was not sustained after the initial euphoria of Alma-Ata. In many cases PHC became a jargon term used as a slogan, and little else. The rhetoric was not backed with the necessary reforms. Agencies were content if countries adopted PHC as a policy, and did not assess actual practice. Politicians saw PHC as a way to reduce expenditure in health and lacked the political will to ensure that services were equitably shared and distributed. Most healthcare resources continue to be directed to the large urban-based hospitals.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Issues of governance and corruption in the use of resources resulted in donors becoming very wary of funding comprehensive, broad-based programs. Vertical, definable, time-limited programs that could be changed every few years suited both donor agencies and governments.</li>
</ul>
<p>*** Field Visit to a nearby PHC site ***</p>
<p>Visit a nearby PHC site and identify:</p>
<ol>
<li>What is the name of the site?</li>
<li>When did the site start?</li>
<li>How many CHWs are active?</li>
<li>What are the PCH services offered?</li>
<li>What are the 10 factors that are making PHC successful in the site?</li>
<li>What are the 10 factors that are making PHC fail in the site?</li>
<li>What are the plans to revitalize PHC activities in the site?</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maternal-and-child-health">Maternal and child health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-and-child-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Understand the concept of facility and community based maternal and child health care</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Outline the goal and focus of MCH and family planning</li>
<li>Describe MCH and family planning services</li>
<li>Describe community base approach to MCT and FP</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Maternal health is the health of women during pregnancy, childbirth, and the postpartum period.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It encompasses the health care dimensions of family planning, preconception, prenatal, and postnatal care in order to reduce maternal morbidity and mortality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preconception care can include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health promotion,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Screening</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>and other interventions among women of reproductive age to reduce risk factors that might affect future pregnancies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Postnatal care issues include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Recovery from childbirth,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Concerns about newborn care,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutrition,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breastfeeding,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family planning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The goal of prenatal care is to:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>o Detect any potential complications of pregnancy early,
o Prevent them if possible,
o Direct the woman to appropriate specialist medical services as appropriate.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Primary areas of focus in MCH include:
o Increasing healthy birth outcomes;
o Promoting and assuring comprehensive primary care for children, including children with special health care needs;
o Promoting healthy lifestyles among school-age youth, ages 6-21, including children with special health care needs;
o Assuring access to safe, healthy child care up to age six, including children with special health care needs;
o Preconception, pregnancy testing and planning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In Africa, one out of 210 mothers dies during pregnancy or delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most maternal deaths are due to causes directly related to:
o Pregnancy
o Childbirth,
o Unsafe abortion
o Obstetric complications such as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe bleeding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypertensive disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obstructed labor
o Other indirect cause like:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Relatively low rate of institutional deliveries,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Due to transport problems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of infrastructure,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Due to cultural prejudices and resistance against giving birth outside the family circle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The fifth Millennium Development Goal (MDG) aims to reduce the maternal mortality ratio by 75% between 1990 and 2015.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In Kenya, maternal mortality remains high at 488 maternal deaths per 100,000 live births.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The MCH/FP clinic is founded on quality and afford-able services that advocate for safe motherhood, proper child development, and a healthy family.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mch-services">MCH Services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mch-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The services offered in MCH clinic are as follows:
o Focused antenatal care.
o Targeted post natal care.
o Providing all family planning methods: short term, long term, permanent i.e. vasectomy &amp; tubal ligation.
o Screening of Breast and Cervical cancer in all women of reproductive ages.
o Giving immunization i.e. BCG, Pentavalent, Polio, Measles.
o Growth monitoring for children under the age of five.
o Counseling and testing of antenatal mothers and partners on PMTCT - eMTC
o Create awareness through Micro teaching on various topics i.e. Nutrition, Breast feeding, Weaning etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunization">Immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The basic principle of immunization is to administer into a healthy person a vaccine that will prevent that person from getting a certain disease.</li>
<li>Vaccines may be of:</li>
<li>Live attenuated: (e.g. Rubella, OPV, Measles and BCG),</li>
<li>Inactivated or killed (e.g. Hib, IPV)</li>
<li>Micro-organisms</li>
<li>Detoxified toxins (e.g. Tetanus)</li>
<li>Generally, several vaccines can be given at the same time. This is important since you do not know when you will see the child again.</li>
<li>BCG, OPV, DPT-HeB-Hib and Measles vaccines can be given simultaneously if the child is of the appropriate age and has not received the early immunizations.</li>
<li>A critically ill child needing hospital admission must be given the appropriate vaccines upon recovery</li>
<li>Remember:</li>
<li>That a slight fever and/or other minor illness should not prevent you from immunizing a child</li>
<li>To inform mothers/child-caretakers about possible side effects of each of the given vaccines</li>
<li>To record all vaccinations on tally sheets and on the Child-Health immunization cards and instruct the mothers always to bring the cards along with them when taking children to a health facility</li>
<li>To instruct mothers to return the child for the next immunization date as indicated on the card</li>
<li>That vaccines are easily destroyed by heat and rendered ineffective</li>
<li>To handle the disposal of used sharp syringes appropriately</li>
<li>To ensure appropriate cold storage of the vaccines and follow the recommended cold-chain instructions for each of the vaccines carefully.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-the-common-vaccine-preventable-diseases">Facts about the common vaccine-preventable diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-the-common-vaccine-preventable-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="whooping-cough-pertussis">Whooping cough (Pertussis):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#whooping-cough-pertussis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A communicable disease.</li>
<li>Spread by droplets.</li>
<li>Symptoms include:</li>
<li>Severe cough followed by a whoop and vomiting, Leads to malnutrition, Can cause death, Severe in under 1 year old.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diphtheria">Diphtheria:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diphtheria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>An infectious disease.</li>
<li>Spread by droplets.</li>
<li>Symptoms include: Difficulty in breathing, Swallowing, Enlarged neck.</li>
<li>Very severe when it occurs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tetanus-see-tetanus">Tetanus: [see tetanus]:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus-see-tetanus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A clinical syndrome involving primarily the central nervous system and resulting from the tetanus toxins.</li>
<li>Enters through open wounds, cuts and umbilical stump.</li>
<li>Symptoms include: Stiffness, Locked jaw, Inability to suckle and muscle spasms.</li>
<li>Has a very high mortality (&gt;50%).</li>
<li>Immunizing pregnant mothers ensures protection of her new born baby.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="measles-rubeola">Measles (Rubeola):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measles-rubeola" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Highly infectious killer disease.
Symptoms include: Rash, Fever, Cough, Red eyes;
Is associated with: blindness, malnutrition, deafness, pneumonia and death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poliomyelitis-infantile-paralysis">Poliomyelitis (Infantile Paralysis):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poliomyelitis-infantile-paralysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An acute communicable disease.
Spread by droplets and oro-faecal contamination.
Symptoms include:
Pain and flaccid paralysis in limbs, fever, vomiting; can lead to permanent deformity, and can cause death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tuberculosis">Tuberculosis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A communicable disease.
Spread by droplet.
Symptoms include: fever, wasting, deep chesty cough, Night sweats, May have lymphadenopathy.
Leads to lowered resistance to other diseases and may be fatal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hepatitis-b">Hepatitis B:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Is a highly infectious disease.
Transmitted mainly by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Parenteral route,</li>
<li>From person to person</li>
<li>By close contact
Through exchange of body fluids such as:</li>
<li>Saliva, Secretions from open wounds, Blood, Vaginal secretions and semen.</li>
</ul>
<p>Transmission between children is common, since they are often more infectious than adults.
Transmission from carrier mothers can occur in up to 80% of babies during the perinatal period,
Infection may be transmitted either:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vertically (transplacentially from mother to unborn baby)</li>
<li>Horizontally by close contact.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="childhood-immunization-schedule-in-kenya">Childhood immunization schedule in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#childhood-immunization-schedule-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Vaccine</th><th>Age</th><th>Remarks</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>BCG POLIO (OPV O)</td><td>At birth</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Birth</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Dose</td><td>Or at first contact with child</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>DPT_{1}-HeB_{1}-Hib_{1}</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>DOSE POLIO (OPV 1)</td><td>6 weeks</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>(1 ½ months)</td><td>Or at first contact with child after that age</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>DPT_{2}-HeB_{2}-Hib_{2}</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>DOSE POLIO (OPV 2)</td><td>10 weeks</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>(2 ½ months)</td><td>4 weeks after DPT 1 and OPV 1 can also be given anytime after this period, when in contact with the child.</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>DPT₃-HeB₃-Hib₃ 14 weeks 4 weeks after DPT 2 and OPV 2 can also be given any time after DOSE POLIO (OPV 3) (3 ½ months) this period, when in contact with the child.</p>
<p>Measles 9 months May be given between 6 and 9 months if child is admitted to hospital for any other illness. Repeat at 9 months as per KEPI schedule.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-schedule-for-pregnant-mothers-tt2">Immunization schedule for pregnant mothers (TT2+)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-schedule-for-pregnant-mothers-tt2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tetanus Toxoid (TT) Pregnant women 1st dose with first pregnancy or subsequent pregnancy</p>
<p>2nd dose - 4 wks after first dose
3rd dose - 6 months after 2nd dose
4th dose - at least 1 year after the third dose
5th dose - at least 1 year after the fourth dose</p>
<p>Immunizing a pregnant mother ensures protection of her newborn baby.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaccine-dosage-and-route-of-administration">VACCINE DOSAGE AND ROUTE OF ADMINISTRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-dosage-and-route-of-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>BCG*</p>
<p>Child under 1 year, 0.05 ml.</p>
<p>Child over 1 year, full dose, 0.1 ml</p>
<p>Intra-dermally into upper outer part of left forearm, at the junction of the upper and middle thirds. If given correctly a small wheal appears at the site of the injection. Inform the mother that a small sore will appear in 2-6 weeks. Let this heal by itself. It will leave a small scar. If no reaction develops, the vaccination should be repeated after 3 months.</p>

<p>Contra-indications. A definite severe reaction to a preceding vaccine dose is a contraindication to further doses.</p>
<p>Live vaccines should not be given to individuals with impaired immune response e.g. leukaemia, HIV/AIDS.</p>
<p>The intramuscular route should not be used in patients with bleeding disorders such as haemophilia or thrombocytopaenia.</p>

<p>Asymptomatic children infected with HIV should receive all standard Kenya Expanded Programme on Immunization (KEPI) vaccines. Non-immunized children with symptomatic HIV infection should receive all standard vaccines except BCG.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-and-adverse-reactions-to-vaccinations">Side-effects and adverse reactions to vaccinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-and-adverse-reactions-to-vaccinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bcg-vaccine">BCG Vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bcg-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="measles-vaccine">Measles Vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measles-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Adverse reactions include fever, mild rash and rarely convulsions, encephalitis and sub-acute schlerosing pan-encephalitis (SSPE).</p>
<p>DPT (Diphtheria, Pertussis, Tetanus)</p>
<p>Most adverse reactions are attributed to the pertussis component. Minor reactions include, pain at the site of injection and fever. Major reactions are persistent crying, high pitched cry, excessive somnolescence, convulsions, encephalopathy and coma.</p>
<p>Recombinant DNA Hepatitis B Vaccine</p>
<p>Side effects include pain, fever and swelling at the site of injection.</p>
<p>Family Planning and Contraceptive methods, types and Options in Kenya</p>
<ul>
<li>The choice of one method of contraception against the other depend on:</li>
<li>individual medical condition</li>
<li>taste of an individual or partner,</li>
<li>The most common method of family planning is hormonal method except condom followed by mechanical methods. The most reliable method is surgical method and the most unreliable method is natural methods.</li>
<li>Type of family planning and contraceptives can largely be divided into four categories</li>
<li>Natural</li>
<li>Barrier</li>
<li>Hormonal</li>
<li>Surgical</li>
</ul>
<p>NATURAL METHODS OF FAMILY PLANNING AND CONTRACEPTIVES METHODS IN KENYA</p>
<ul>
<li>It is called natural because it does not involve use of drug or device</li>
<li>The following are the available method or types of natural family planning methods</li>
<li>The following make up natural family planning methods:</li>
<li>Withdrawal Method (coitus interrupters)</li>
<li>Warning this method can only be used in highly motivated couples.</li>
<li>It is useful as a temporary method for example supplies for of regular method are not available or the couples are together for only a short time.</li>
<li>Safe period (rhythm method)</li>
<li>This one means that couples avoid sex the time the woman eggs (ovum) are ready for fertilization.</li>
<li>This is around mid-month of a woman's circle.</li>
<li>This means that there should no sex for the couples who are using this method between day 8(eight) and day 20 (twenty) of a woman's circle i.e. a total of 12 days without sex in a month.</li>
<li>Have you ever seen a cow on heat? Unfortunately this is the period at which women folks are on heat so this method like the withdrawal method require highly motivated couples</li>
<li>Breastfeeding amenorrhea method</li>
<li>Risk of pregnancy in exclusively breastfeeding couples in the first 6 (six) months so long as the woman has not experienced menses is 2% (percent)</li>
<li>It is a reliable method so long as the above conditions are intact.</li>
<li>Cervical mucus membrane</li>
</ul>

<p>&gt; This is a slightly technical method and couples are advised against using this if they don't understand the physiology of ovulation.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Basal body temperature (BBT) method</strong>
&gt; Like cervical mucus membrane this is also a slightly cumbersome method because it involve daily recording of a chart.
&gt; Check the temperature five minutes before waking up and enter in ascertain chart after woman's eggs are released (ovulation) temperature rises by (0.2 – 0.6) C intercourse should be avoided when the temperature is low and resumed when the temperature has risen up next period.
&gt; like you might have noticed this method is very unreliable form of family planning, what if one gets sick an the temperature rises, what if one fails to record the temperature.
&gt; This method can be easily manipulated by women folk to deny men folks there conjugal rights by just manipulating the temperatures.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note: Natural family planning requires high motivation and so makes them not particularly reliable method of family planning.</p>
<hr>
<p><strong>BARRIER METHODS OF CONTRACEPTION AND FAMILY PLANNING IN KENYA</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>These method or type of family planning include:</li>
<li>Male and Female Condoms</li>
<li>Spermicides</li>
<li>Diaphragms</li>
<li>Cervical Caps</li>
<li>Whereas condoms, diaphragms, and cervical caps are mechanical barriers, spermicides are chemicals that interfere with the movement of the sperm and its ability to fertilise the egg.</li>
<li>Currently in Kenya, the use of diaphragms, cervical caps, and spermicides is negligible.</li>
<li>In addition, scientific evidence has shown that repeated and high-dose use of the spermicide might cause vaginal and cervical irritation or abrasions, which could increase the risk of infection with HIV.</li>
</ul>
<hr>
<p><strong>HORMONAL METHODS OF FAMILY PLANNING AND CONTRACEPTIVE METHODS IN KENYA</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>This is the most commonly used method or type of family planning and contraceptive after condom</li>
<li>They include hormone taken orally, by injection or implanted to prevent development and maturation of woman's eggs (ovum's)</li>
<li>Common hormonal FP and contraceptives methods are:
&gt; Emergency contraception ( e-pills )
&gt; Ordinary pills
&gt; Injectable contraceptives
&gt; Contraceptive Implants (Jadelle, Implanon, Zarin)
&gt; Hormone-releasing intrauterine systems</li>
<li>This method involves use of devices which may sometime have some form of drug (hormone) attached to it,</li>
<li>Their mode of function is by placing a barrier so that sperm does not get into the fallopian tube to fertilize the woman's egg.</li>
<li>The following are the available IUCD type of family planning and contraceptives methods in Kenya</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="voluntary-surgical-contraception">VOLUNTARY SURGICAL CONTRACEPTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#voluntary-surgical-contraception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-based-maternal-newborn-and-child-health-services">Community-Based Maternal, Newborn and Child Health Services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-based-maternal-newborn-and-child-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Aims to reduce the number of deaths among mothers, newborns, and young children by improving the health services available in four rural districts</li>
<li>Provides women with greater access to good-quality, reliable health services.</li>
<li>It helps to ensure that district health facilities offer essential health services for women and children;</li>
<li>It provides training for health care workers in emergency care for pregnant women, new mothers, and newborn babies;</li>
<li>It strengthens the management and supervision practices in health care facilities.</li>
<li>It improves the ability of men and women in the communities to recognize, prevent, and respond to maternal and child health issues.</li>
<li>The community MCH services include:</li>
<li>Organizing community events and mass media campaigns,</li>
<li>Training community theatre groups,</li>
<li>Selecting peer youth educators and male champions to raise awareness about potential health issues;</li>
<li>Conducting home visits to provide pre-natal and post-natal care and care for newborns and young children;</li>
<li>Equipping community health workers to provide services in remote areas and to refer patients to health centres where necessary.</li>
<li>It emphasises the role that men can play in helping to improve the health of women and children.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="growth-monitoring">Growth Monitoring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#growth-monitoring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition-and-health">Nutrition and Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition-and-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal: Increase understanding on nutrition in the context of community health</p>
<p>Specific objectives:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe nutrition and dietary requirements in our lives</li>
<li>Describe the implications of malnutrition in health and development</li>
</ul>
<p>Nutrition - Nutrition is the intake of food, considered in relation to the body's dietary needs. Good nutrition is an adequate, well balanced diet combined with regular physical activity. It is the cornerstone of good health. Poor nutrition can lead to reduced immunity, increased susceptibility to disease, impaired physical and mental development, and reduced productivity. Eating well is important for everyone's health and wellbeing and is vital for preventing chronic disease in later life.</p>
<p>Community nutrition – is the nutrition in the context of community. In order for nutrition to have impact on human health and well-being, it must be applied to human populations through community and population based intervention and education programs.</p>
<p>Malnutrition - Malnutrition is the condition that develops when the body does not get the right amount of the vitamins, minerals, and other nutrients it needs to maintain healthy tissues and organ function. It is a cause and consequence of ill health across many groups; however, older people tend to be more vulnerable to this condition, which can severely impact on health outcomes and quality of life.</p>
<p>Basic nutrition - Basic nutrition is the food intake, dietary nutrients required during our phases of life</p>
<ul>
<li>Food intake – An average person takes at least 3 meals in a day (breakfast, lunch and supper). People tend to have supplementary feeds in between the main meals. Children are required to be fed every time according to their demand. Food intake is influenced by income, appetite, exposure to food and social status.</li>
<li>Dietary nutrients – Our body requires essential dietary nutrients for its normal function. The nutrient requirements are: Carbohydrates, Proteins, Water, Vitamins, and Minerals. Essential nutrient are substance that must be obtained from the diet because the body cannot make it in sufficient quantity to meet its needs. In establishing dietary requirements the goal is to determine what amount is high enough, if ingested routinely, to prevent impairment of health even if intake becomes inadequate for a short period</li>
<li>Nutrition during phases of life – This is the nutrition required during: Pregnancy and early childhood; Childhood and adolescent; School going age; Adults; and Older age.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Pregnancy and early childhood - Starting early with breastfeeding and providing good nutrition for children gives the best start to a healthy life. Good nutrition in pregnancy is essential for keeping a developing baby and mother healthy. Breastfeeding is the natural way to feed babies. Breastfeeding is extremely important for the health outcomes of infants and their mother. Not breastfeeding is associated with adverse health outcomes for both mothers and infants, ranging from infectious illness to chronic diseases later in life. Solids should be introduced at around six months of age when the infant is developmentally ready. For young children, a healthy diet is required for optimal growth and development. It can also help to improve concentration, fight illnesses, and prevent long term health complications.</p>
<p>&gt; Children and Adolescents - Children and adolescents need sufficient foods to grow and develop normally. Growth should be checked regularly for young children. Physical activity is important for children and adolescents. Many infants suffer and die because of ignorance, meanness of parents and inability to understand the infant communication language
&gt; School aged children - Childhood is an important period when children develop the knowledge, skills and behaviors for lifelong health and wellbeing. We know that education and health are inseparable and that a healthy child learns well.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Adults - Healthy eating during adulthood is vital for effective functioning of body systems and immunity, maintaining a healthy weight, and preventing and managing chronic conditions such as diabetes and heart disease.
&gt; Older people - Good nutrition is important for older people to help promote independence and to reduce illness and premature death. Maintaining a healthy lifestyle, including good nutrition, plays an important role in ensuring older people can live well at home for longer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-community-nutrition">Components of community nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-community-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Community nutrition entails the following components:</p>
<ul>
<li>Surveillance of food chain – This is assessing food for possible infestation with germs, toxic. It’s also called food contamination monitoring</li>
<li>Nutritional epidemiology - A <strong>medical research</strong> that studies the relationship between <strong>nutrition</strong> and health. It is the on effects of dietary intake and nutritional status on health of individual or community. Multiple nutrients work together in the body, with differing impacts on different systems and under differing environmental conditions.</li>
<li>Clinical nutrition and diabetes - The number of patients with diabetes is growing rapidly. Involves assessing the effectiveness of <strong>clinical nutrition</strong> in diabetes care and outcomes</li>
<li>Nutrition education - Is any combination of educational strategies, accompanied by environmental supports, designed to facilitate voluntary adoption of food choices and nutrition-related behaviors conducive to health and well-being. Nutrition education is delivered through multiple venues and involves activities at the individual, community, and policy levels</li>
<li>Food and nutrition policy – It makes healthy food more available; Discloses the calorie content of restaurant foods; Teach people how to make healthy eating easier. There are 3 existing nutrition policies and programs, like: Nutrition Facts labels on packaged foods; Nutrition standards for school lunches; Regulation of food additives.</li>
<li>Food industry and standard agency - is a complex, global collective of diverse businesses that supply much of the food and food energy consumed by the world population e.g. UNILIVER. The Food Standards Agency is concerned with the whole food industry – from farming, food production and distribution, to retail and catering. It addresses food safety issues at every stage of the chain, providing information and guidance on best practice and legal requirements.</li>
<li>Mass catering - Food and drink supplied by a caterer to large numbers of customers at the same time</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="malnutrition">Malnutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Individuals are malnourished, or suffer from under nutrition if their diet does not provide them with adequate calories and protein for maintenance and growth, or they cannot fully utilize the food they eat due to illness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Growth failure malnutrition, as the name suggests, is the failure of an individual to grow as expected in stature or weight, according to his/her age and gender. Growth failure malnutrition can take three serious types:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acute malnutrition or wasting arises out of sudden, drastic weight loss. It leads to three clinical malnutrition types:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Marasmus: this occurs when body fat and tissues degenerate at an alarming rate to compensate for the lack of nutrients. As a result, the body’s internal processes begin to slow down alarmingly fast as does the activity of the immune system.
&gt; Kwashiorkor: this is characterized by bilateral pitting oedema (fluid retention) in the legs and feet. As a result, the under-nourished child may actually look plump.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Marasmic-kwashiorkor: This is characterized by both severe wasting and oedema.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Chronic malnutrition or stunting happens over a long period of time and has more long-lasting consequences. It begins before birth due to poor maternal health and leads to stunted growth in an otherwise normally proportioned child. Poor breast feeding, infections and lack of availability of proper nutrients are the main causes behind it. Stunting is dangerous because it becomes irreversible after an age. Therefore, it becomes important to nip it in the bud by providing proper medical treatment to pregnant women and young girls.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Micronutrient malnutrition implies a moderate to severe lack of Vitamins A, B, C and D, Calcium, Folate, Iodine, Iron, Zinc and Selenium. These vitamins and minerals are of utmost importance in various body processes and their deficiency can make an otherwise healthy person malnourished:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iron deficiency causes anaemia, poor brain development and cardiac functioning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iodine deficiency leads to impaired thyroid functioning and mental retardation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vitamin D deficiency causes rickets and other bone development related disorders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Selenium deficiency leads to poor cardiac function, weak immunity and osteoarthritis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vitamin A deficiency is a cause of poor vision, bone development and immunity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vitamin B12 deficiency leads to nerve degeneration and poor RBC formation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Folate or vitamin B9 deficiency causes slow growth and anemia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Zinc deficiency can cause poor immunity, sensory perception and anemia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Signs and symptoms of malnutrition- A symptom is something the patient feels and reports, while a sign is something other people, such as the doctor detect. For example, pain may be a symptom while a rash may be a sign. The general signs and symptoms include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss of fat (adipose tissue)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breathing difficulties, a higher risk of respiratory failure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Depression</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Higher risk of complications after surgery and lower healing hence longer recovery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Higher risk of hypothermia - abnormally feeling cold and low body temperature</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The total number of some types of white blood cells falls; consequently, the immune system is weakened, increasing the risk of infections.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lower sex drive and problems with fertility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduced muscle and tissue mass</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tiredness, fatigue, apathy and irritability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In more severe cases:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skin may become thin, dry, inelastic, pale, and cold</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eventually, as fat in the face is lost, the cheeks look hollow and the eyes sunken</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hair becomes dry and sparse, falling out easily</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sometimes, severe malnutrition may lead to unresponsiveness (stupor)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If calorie deficiency continues for long enough, there may be heart, liver and respiratory failure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Total starvation is said to be fatal within 8 to 12 weeks</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Causes of malnutrition are:</li>
<li>Poor diet - if a person does not eat enough food, or if what they eat does not provide them with the nutrients they require for good health, they suffer from malnutrition. Poor diet may be caused by one of several different factors. If the patient develops dysphagia (swallowing difficulties) because of an illness, or when recovering from an illness, they may not be able to consume enough of the right nutrients.</li>
<li>Mental health problems - some patients with mental health conditions, such as depression, may develop eating habits which lead to malnutrition. Patients with anorexia nervosa or bulimia may develop malnutrition because they are ingesting too little food.</li>
<li>Mobility problems - people with mobility problems may suffer from malnutrition simply because they either cannot get out enough to buy foods, or find preparing them too arduous.</li>
<li>Digestive disorders and stomach conditions - some people may eat properly, but their bodies cannot absorb the nutrients they need for good health.</li>
<li>Alcoholism - this is a chronic (long-term) disease. Individuals who suffer from alcoholism can develop gastritis, or pancreas damage. These problems also seriously undermine the body's ability to digest food, absorb certain vitamins, and produce hormones which regulate metabolism. Alcohol contains calories, reducing the patient's feeling of hunger, so he/she consequently may not eat enough proper food to supply the body with essential nutrients.</li>
<li>Food shortage, price and distribution</li>
<li>Lack of breastfeeding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="impact-of-malnutrition-on-health-and-development">Impact of Malnutrition on Health and Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#impact-of-malnutrition-on-health-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Malnutrition and starvation have devastating impact on children, adults and especially on pregnant women. They also have severe and far-reaching socio-economic impacts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Effects on children - Mental retardation, stunted growth, poor immune system, micronutrient deficiency, GI tract infections, anemia and inevitably – death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Effects on pregnant women - Besides the health of the child being poor, a pregnant woman might have difficult labour, postpartum hemorrhage and anemia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>General effects - Weak immunity, inactivity of muscles, apathy, depression, and kidney function impairment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malnourished children experience developmental delays, weight-loss and illness as a result of inadequate intake of protein, calories and other nutrients. Because orphaned and institutionalized children may experience one or several macronutrient and micronutrient deficiencies, they are at risk for a variety of short-term and long-term complications:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Short-Term Implications - Because so much development occurs in the first few years of life, nutrient deficiencies can have major short-term implications in young children.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immune Implications - Malnourishment can greatly compromise a child's immune system, making them more susceptible to infectious diseases. Particularly in institutions where there are poor sanitary practices, children are vulnerable to infections from other children or caregivers.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Growth Implications - A child may contract an infection due to poor nutritional status. In turn, a gastrointestinal infection places the child at even greater risk for nutrient deficiencies because nutrients are unable to be absorbed properly. Consequently, nutrient deficiency combined with infection can cause growth retardation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Additionally, a deficiency in one nutrient may lead to a deficiency in another nutrient. For example, deficiencies in iron, magnesium and zinc can cause anorexia and thereby result in reduced intake of other important nutrients such as protein. Low lipid intake can also affect the absorption of important fat-soluble vitamins such as vitamins A and Zinc and protein deficiencies can retard bone growth and development, putting a child at risk for long-term complications.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>o Long-Term Implications - The short-term implications of malnutrition eventually give way to long-term complications, such as growth and cognitive delays:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Growth Implications - Malnutrition not only impacts growth in the short term, but can also limit total bone growth. Additionally, children classified as low height-for-age (stunted) may never be able to regain lost growth potential if they continue to live in a nutritionally deprived situation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cognitive Implications - Malnutrition negatively effects brain development causing delays in motor and cognitive development, such as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attention deficit disorder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning disabilities and impaired school performance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decreased IQ scores</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Memory deficiency</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduced social skills</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reduced language development</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><em><strong>Field practice</strong></em></p>
<p>Group1. Surveillance of food chain</p>
<ol>
<li>What methods can you adopt in assessing food for possible infestation with germs, toxic?</li>
<li>Develop a food contamination monitoring questionnaire</li>
<li>Use the questionnaire to assess foodstuff in a local market</li>
</ol>
<p>Group2. Nutritional epidemiology</p>
<ol>
<li>Identify all the relationship between nutrition and health</li>
<li>Develop a food frequency assessment tool</li>
<li>Use the tool to assess the food frequency among pupils attending a local primary school</li>
</ol>
<p>Group3. Clinical nutrition and diabetes</p>
<ol>
<li>Develop a dummy table eliciting cases of diabetes by age and sex</li>
<li>Use the dummy table to capture the number of diabetes cases in a nearby hospital for 5 months</li>
<li>Randomize 10 cases of diabetes notes and assess presence of nutritional therapy</li>
</ol>
<p>Group4. Nutrition education</p>
<ol>
<li>Identify communication strategies that would be suitable in promoting adoption of food choice and nutritional behaviors</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Use the communication strategy to sensitize 5 mothers with children having malnutrition related conditions in a pediatric ward in a nearby hospital</li>
<li>Use your mobile phone to take a picture of sensitization session going on</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="group5-food-and-nutrition-policy">Group5. Food and nutrition policy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group5-food-and-nutrition-policy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="group6-food-industry-and-standard-agency">Group6. Food industry and standard agency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group6-food-industry-and-standard-agency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<ul>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="group7-mass-catering">Group7. Mass catering<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group7-mass-catering" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
